He argued that there was nothing surprising in "the fact that the Soviet Union, anxious for its future safety, \[was\] trying to see to it that governments loyal in their attitude to the Soviet Union should exist in these countries."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarxists_Internet_Archive_107-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarxists_Internet_Archive-107">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCauley2008143_108-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCauley2008143-108">[102]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Cold_war_europe_military_alliances_map_en.png/200px-Cold_war_europe_military_alliances_map_en.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cold_war_europe_military_alliances_map_en.png)

European military alliances

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Cold_war_europe_economic_alliances_map_en.png/200px-Cold_war_europe_economic_alliances_map_en.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cold_war_europe_economic_alliances_map_en.png)

European economic blocs

Soviet territorial demands to Turkey regarding the Dardanelles in the [Turkish Straits crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Straits_crisis "Turkish Straits crisis") and Black Sea [border disputes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_territorial_claims_against_Turkey "Soviet territorial claims against Turkey") were also a major factor in increasing tensions.<sup id="cite_ref-109"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-109">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHasanli2014221–222_102-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHasanli2014221%E2%80%93222-102">[96]</a></sup> In September, the Soviet side produced the [Novikov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikolai_Vasilevich_Novikov "Nikolai Vasilevich Novikov") telegram, sent by the Soviet ambassador to the US but commissioned and "co-authored" by [Vyacheslav Molotov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vyacheslav_Molotov "Vyacheslav Molotov"); it portrayed the US as being in the grip of monopoly capitalists who were building up military capability "to prepare the conditions for winning world supremacy in a new war".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKydd2018107_110-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKydd2018107-110">[104]</a></sup> On 6 September 1946, [James F. Byrnes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_F._Byrnes "James F. Byrnes") delivered a [speech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Restatement_of_Policy_on_Germany "Restatement of Policy on Germany") in Germany repudiating the [Morgenthau Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morgenthau_Plan "Morgenthau Plan") (a proposal to partition and de-industrialize post-war Germany) and warning the Soviets that the US intended to maintain a military presence in Europe indefinitely.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200530_111-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200530-111">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-112">[106]</a></sup> As Byrnes stated a month later, "The nub of our program was to win the German people ... it was a battle between us and Russia over minds ..." In December, the Soviets agreed to withdraw from Iran after persistent US pressure, an early success of containment policy.

By 1947, US president [Harry S. Truman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_S._Truman "Harry S. Truman") was outraged by the perceived resistance of the Soviet Union to American demands in Iran, Turkey, and Greece, as well as Soviet rejection of the [Baruch Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baruch_Plan "Baruch Plan") on nuclear weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMilestones:_1945–1952_113-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilestones:_1945%E2%80%931952-113">[107]</a></sup> In February 1947, the British government announced that it could no longer afford to finance the [Kingdom of Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Greece "Kingdom of Greece") in [its civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_Civil_War "Greek Civil War") against Communist-led insurgents.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIatrides1996373–376_114-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIatrides1996373%E2%80%93376-114">[108]</a></sup> In the same month, Stalin conducted the rigged [1947 Polish legislative election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947_Polish_legislative_election "1947 Polish legislative election") which constituted an open breach of the [Yalta Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yalta_Agreement "Yalta Agreement"). The [US government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States "Federal government of the United States") responded to this announcement by adopting a policy of [containment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Containment "Containment"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200528–29_115-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200528%E2%80%9329-115">[109]</a></sup> with the goal of stopping the spread of [communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communism "Communism"). Truman delivered a speech calling for the allocation of $400 million to intervene in the war and unveiled the [Truman Doctrine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truman_Doctrine "Truman Doctrine"), which framed the conflict as a contest between free peoples and [totalitarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Totalitarian "Totalitarian") regimes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200528–29_115-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200528%E2%80%9329-115">[109]</a></sup> American policymakers accused the Soviet Union of conspiring against the Greek royalists in an effort to [expand Soviet influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domino_theory "Domino theory") even though Stalin had told the Communist Party to cooperate with the British-backed government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGerolymatos2017195–204_116-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGerolymatos2017195%E2%80%93204-116">[110]</a></sup> (The insurgents were helped by [Josip Broz Tito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito "Josip Broz Tito")'s [Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia "Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia") against Stalin's wishes.)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194–197_117-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194%E2%80%93197-117">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200538_118-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200538-118">[112]</a></sup>

Enunciation of the Truman Doctrine marked the beginning of a US bipartisan defense and foreign policy consensus between [Republicans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States) "Republican Party (United States)") and [Democrats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States) "Democratic Party (United States)") focused on containment and [deterrence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deterrence_theory "Deterrence theory") that weakened during and after the [Vietnam War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam_War "Vietnam War"), but ultimately persisted thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPaterson198935,_142,_212_119-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPaterson198935,_142,_212-119">[113]</a></sup> Moderate and conservative parties in Europe, as well as social democrats, gave virtually unconditional support to the Western alliance,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoschonas200221_120-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoschonas200221-120">[114]</a></sup> while [European](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurocommunism "Eurocommunism") and [American Communists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_USA "Communist Party USA"), financed by the [KGB](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KGB "KGB") and involved in its intelligence operations,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAndrewMitrokhin2000276_121-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAndrewMitrokhin2000276-121">[115]</a></sup> adhered to Moscow's line, although dissent began to appear after 1956. Other critiques of the consensus policy came from [anti-Vietnam War activists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposition_to_United_States_involvement_in_the_Vietnam_War "Opposition to United States involvement in the Vietnam War"), the [Campaign for Nuclear Disarmament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Campaign_for_Nuclear_Disarmament "Campaign for Nuclear Disarmament"), and the [anti-nuclear movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-nuclear_movement "Anti-nuclear movement").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrockerHampsonAall200755_122-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrockerHampsonAall200755-122">[116]</a></sup>

### Marshall Plan, Czechoslovak coup d'état, and formation of two German states

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Marshall_Plan.png/200px-Marshall_Plan.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Marshall_Plan.png)

Map of Cold War-era Europe and the [Near East](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Near_East "Near East") showing countries that received Marshall Plan aid. The red columns show the relative amount of total aid received per nation.

In early 1947, France, Britain and the United States unsuccessfully attempted to reach an agreement with the Soviet Union for a plan envisioning an economically self-sufficient Germany, including a detailed accounting of the industrial plants, goods and infrastructure already taken by the Soviets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200016_123-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200016-123">[117]</a></sup> In June 1947, in accordance with the [Truman Doctrine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truman_Doctrine "Truman Doctrine"), the United States enacted the [Marshall Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshall_Plan "Marshall Plan"), a pledge of economic assistance for all European countries willing to participate, including the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200016_123-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200016-123">[117]</a></sup> Under the plan, which President Harry S. Truman signed on 3 April 1948, the US government gave to Western European countries over $13 billion (equivalent to $189.39 billion in 2016) to rebuild the [economy of Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_Europe "Economy of Europe"). Later, the program led to the creation of the [OECD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD").

The plan's aim was to rebuild the democratic and economic systems of Europe and to counter perceived threats to the [European balance of power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_balance_of_power "European balance of power"), such as communist parties seizing control through revolutions or elections.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis1990186_124-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis1990186-124">[118]</a></sup> The plan also stated that European prosperity was contingent upon German economic recovery.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDinan201740_125-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDinan201740-125">[119]</a></sup> One month later, Truman signed the [National Security Act of 1947](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Security_Act_of_1947 "National Security Act of 1947"), creating a unified [Department of Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense "United States Department of Defense"), the [Central Intelligence Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency "Central Intelligence Agency") (CIA), and the [National Security Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_National_Security_Council "United States National Security Council") (NSC). These would become the main bureaucracies for US defense policy in the Cold War.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916_126-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916-126">[120]</a></sup>

Stalin believed that economic integration with the West would allow [Eastern Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc") countries to escape Soviet control, and that the US was trying to buy a pro-US re-alignment of Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200532_127-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200532-127">[121]</a></sup> Stalin therefore prevented Eastern Bloc nations from receiving Marshall Plan aid.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200532_127-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200532-127">[121]</a></sup> The Soviet Union's alternative to the Marshall Plan, which was purported to involve Soviet subsidies and trade with central and eastern Europe, became known as the [Molotov Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molotov_Plan "Molotov Plan") (later institutionalized in January 1949 as the [Council for Mutual Economic Assistance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comecon "Comecon")).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194–197_117-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194%E2%80%93197-117">[111]</a></sup> Stalin was also fearful of a reconstituted Germany; his vision of a post-war Germany did not include the ability to rearm or pose any kind of threat to the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005105–106_128-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005105%E2%80%93106-128">[122]</a></sup>

In early 1948, following reports of strengthening "reactionary elements", Czech Communists executed a [coup d'état](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Czechoslovak_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1948 Czechoslovak coup d'état") in [Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovakia "Czechoslovakia") (resulting in the formation of the [Czechoslovak Socialist Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic "Czechoslovak Socialist Republic") (9 May 1948)), the only Eastern Bloc state that the Soviets had permitted to retain democratic structures.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWettig200886_129-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWettig200886-129">[123]</a></sup> The public brutality of the coup shocked Western powers more than any event up to that point, set in motion a brief scare that war would occur, and swept away the last vestiges of opposition to the Marshall Plan in the United States Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200019_130-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200019-130">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrenville2005370–371_131-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrenville2005370%E2%80%93371-131">[125]</a></sup>

In an immediate aftermath of the crisis, the [London Six-Power Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_Six-Power_Conference "London Six-Power Conference") was held, resulting in the [Soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") boycott of the Allied Control Council and its incapacitation, an event marking the beginning of the full-blown Cold War and the end of its prelude, as well as ending any hopes at the time for a single German government and leading to formation in 1949 of the [Federal Republic of Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Germany "West Germany") and [German Democratic Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWettig200896–100_132-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWettig200896%E2%80%93100-132">[126]</a></sup>

## Open hostility and escalation (1948–1962)

The twin policies of the Truman Doctrine and the Marshall Plan led to billions in economic and military aid for Western Europe, Greece, and Turkey. With the US assistance, the Greek military [won its civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_Civil_War "Greek Civil War").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916_126-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916-126">[120]</a></sup> Under the leadership of [Alcide De Gasperi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alcide_De_Gasperi "Alcide De Gasperi") the Italian [Christian Democrats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy) "Christian Democracy (Italy)") defeated the powerful [Communist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Communist_Party "Italian Communist Party")–[Socialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Socialist_Party "Italian Socialist Party") alliance in the [elections of 1948](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Italian_general_election "1948 Italian general election").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005162_133-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005162-133">[127]</a></sup>

### Espionage

All major powers engaged in espionage, using a great variety of spies, [double agents](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_agent "Double agent"), [moles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mole_(espionage) "Mole (espionage)"), and new technologies such as the tapping of telephone cables.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGarthoff2004_134-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarthoff2004-134">[128]</a></sup> The Soviet [KGB](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KGB "KGB") ("Committee for State Security"), the bureau responsible for foreign espionage and internal surveillance, was famous for its effectiveness. The most famous Soviet operation involved its [atomic spies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_spies "Atomic spies") that delivered crucial information from the United States' [Manhattan Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan_Project "Manhattan Project"), leading the USSR to detonate its first nuclear weapon in 1949, four years after the American detonation and much sooner than expected.<sup id="cite_ref-135"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-135">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-136">[130]</a></sup> A massive network of informants throughout the Soviet Union was used to monitor dissent from official Soviet politics and morals.<sup id="cite_ref-137"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-137">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-138">[132]</a></sup> Although to an extent [disinformation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disinformation "Disinformation") had always existed, the term itself was invented, and the strategy formalized by a [black propaganda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_propaganda "Black propaganda") department of the Soviet KGB.<sup id="cite_ref-jowett_139-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-jowett-139">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-140">[134]</a></sup>

Based on the amount of top-secret Cold War archival information that has been released, historian [Raymond L. Garthoff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raymond_L._Garthoff "Raymond L. Garthoff") concludes there probably was parity in the quantity and quality of secret information obtained by each side. However, the Soviets probably had an advantage in terms of [HUMINT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_intelligence_(intelligence_gathering) "Human intelligence (intelligence gathering)") (human intelligence or interpersonal espionage) and "sometimes in its reach into high policy circles." In terms of decisive impact, however, he concludes:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGarthoff200429–30_141-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarthoff200429%E2%80%9330-141">[135]</a></sup>

We also can now have high confidence in the judgment that there were no successful "moles" at the political decision-making level on either side. Similarly, there is no evidence, on either side, of any major political or military decision that was prematurely discovered through espionage and thwarted by the other side. There also is no evidence of any major political or military decision that was crucially influenced (much less generated) by an agent of the other side.

According to historian Robert Louis Benson, "Washington's forte was ['signals' intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Signals_intelligence "Signals intelligence")\--the procurement and analysis of coded foreign messages." leading to the [Venona project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venona_project "Venona project") or Venona intercepts, which monitored the communications of Soviet intelligence agents.<sup id="cite_ref-benson_142-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-benson-142">[136]</a></sup> [Moynihan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daniel_Patrick_Moynihan "Daniel Patrick Moynihan") wrote that the Venona project contained "overwhelming proof of the activities of Soviet spy networks in America, complete with names, dates, places, and deeds."<sup id="cite_ref-:4_143-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-:4-143">[137]</a></sup> The Venona project was kept highly secret even from policymakers until the [Moynihan Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moynihan_Commission_on_Government_Secrecy "Moynihan Commission on Government Secrecy") in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_143-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-:4-143">[137]</a></sup> Despite this, the decryption project had already been betrayed and dispatched to the USSR by [Kim Philby](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Philby "Kim Philby") and [Bill Weisband](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Weisband "Bill Weisband") in 1946,<sup id="cite_ref-:4_143-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-:4-143">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_144-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-:0-144">[138]</a></sup> as was discovered by the US by 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-benson2_145-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-benson2-145">[139]</a></sup> Nonetheless, the Soviets had to keep their discovery of the program secret, too, and continued leaking their own information, some of which was still useful to the American program.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_144-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-:0-144">[138]</a></sup> According to Moynihan, even President Truman may not have been fully informed of Venona, which may have left him unaware of the extent of Soviet espionage.<sup id="cite_ref-trumanfas_146-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-trumanfas-146">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-147">[141]</a></sup>

Clandestine [atomic spies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_spies "Atomic spies") from the Soviet Union, who infiltrated the [Manhattan Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan_Project "Manhattan Project") at various points during WWII, played a major role in increasing tensions that led to the Cold War.<sup id="cite_ref-benson_142-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-benson-142">[136]</a></sup>

In addition to usual espionage, the Western agencies paid special attention to debriefing [Eastern Bloc defectors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emigration_from_the_Eastern_Bloc "Emigration from the Eastern Bloc").<sup id="cite_ref-148"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-148">[142]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Template:Harvard_citation_documentation#Wikilink_to_citation_does_not_work" title="Template:Harvard citation documentation"><span title="Template:Harvard citation documentation#Wikilink to citation does not work">citation not found</span></a></i>]</sup> [Edward Jay Epstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Jay_Epstein "Edward Jay Epstein") describes that the CIA understood that the KGB used "provocations", or fake defections, as a trick to embarrass Western intelligence and establish Soviet double agents. As a result, from 1959 to 1973, the CIA required that East Bloc defectors went through a counterintelligence investigation before being recruited as a source of intelligence.<sup id="cite_ref-149"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-149">[143]</a></sup>

During the late 1970s and 1980s, the KGB perfected its use of espionage to sway and distort diplomacy.<sup id="cite_ref-150"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-150">[144]</a></sup> [Active measures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Active_measures "Active measures") were "clandestine operations designed to further Soviet foreign policy goals," consisting of disinformation, forgeries, leaks to foreign media, and the channeling of aid to militant groups.<sup id="cite_ref-151"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-151">[145]</a></sup> Retired KGB Major General [Oleg Kalugin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oleg_Kalugin "Oleg Kalugin"), former head of Foreign Counter Intelligence for the KGB (1973–1979), described active measures as "the heart and soul of [Soviet intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_historical_secret_police_organizations#Soviet_Union "List of historical secret police organizations")."<sup id="cite_ref-Kalugin_152-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-Kalugin-152">[146]</a></sup>

During the [Sino-Soviet split](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split "Sino-Soviet split"), "spy wars" also occurred between the USSR and PRC.<sup id="cite_ref-153"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-153">[147]</a></sup>

### Cominform and the Tito–Stalin Split

In September 1947, the Soviets created [Cominform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cominform "Cominform") to impose orthodoxy within the international communist movement and tighten political control over Soviet [satellites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satellite_state#Soviet_Union "Satellite state") through coordination of communist parties in the [Eastern Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200532_127-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200532-127">[121]</a></sup> Cominform faced an embarrassing setback the following June, when the [Tito–Stalin split](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tito%E2%80%93Stalin_split "Tito–Stalin split") obliged its members to expel Yugoslavia, which remained communist but adopted a [non-aligned](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement "Non-Aligned Movement") position and began accepting financial aid from the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPapathanasiou201766_154-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPapathanasiou201766-154">[148]</a></sup>

Besides Berlin, the status of the city of [Trieste](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trieste "Trieste") was at issue. Until the break between Tito and Stalin, the Western powers and the Eastern bloc faced each other uncompromisingly. In addition to capitalism and communism, Italians and Slovenes, monarchists and republicans as well as war winners and losers often faced each other irreconcilably. The neutral buffer state [Free Territory of Trieste](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_Territory_of_Trieste "Free Territory of Trieste"), founded in 1947 with the United Nations, was split up and dissolved in 1954 and 1975, also because of the détente between the West and Tito.<sup id="cite_ref-155"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-155">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-156">[150]</a></sup>

### Berlin Blockade and Airlift

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/C-47s_at_Tempelhof_Airport_Berlin_1948.jpg/220px-C-47s_at_Tempelhof_Airport_Berlin_1948.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:C-47s_at_Tempelhof_Airport_Berlin_1948.jpg)

American C-47s unloading at [Tempelhof Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_Tempelhof_Airport "Berlin Tempelhof Airport") in Berlin during the Berlin Blockade

The United States and Britain merged their western German occupation zones into ["Bizonia"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bizone "Bizone") (1 January 1947, later "Trizonia" with the addition of France's zone, April 1949).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200013_157-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200013-157">[151]</a></sup> As part of the economic rebuilding of Germany, in early 1948, representatives of a number of Western European governments and the United States announced an agreement for a merger of western German areas into a federal governmental system.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200018_158-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200018-158">[152]</a></sup> In addition, in accordance with the [Marshall Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshall_Plan "Marshall Plan"), they began to re-industrialize and rebuild the West German economy, including the introduction of a new [Deutsche Mark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsche_Mark "Deutsche Mark") currency to replace the old [Reichsmark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reichsmark "Reichsmark") currency that the Soviets had debased.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200031_159-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200031-159">[153]</a></sup> The US had secretly decided that a unified and neutral Germany was undesirable, with [Walter Bedell Smith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_Bedell_Smith "Walter Bedell Smith") telling General Eisenhower "in spite of our announced position, we really do not want nor intend to accept German unification on any terms that the Russians might agree to, even though they seem to meet most of our requirements."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELayne200767_160-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELayne200767-160">[154]</a></sup>

Shortly thereafter, Stalin instituted the [Berlin Blockade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_Blockade "Berlin Blockade") (24 June 1948 – 12 May 1949), one of the first major crises of the Cold War, preventing Western food, materials and supplies from arriving in the West Germany's exclave of [West Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Berlin "West Berlin").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200533_161-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200533-161">[155]</a></sup> The United States (primarily), Britain, France, Canada, Australia, New Zealand, and several other countries began the massive "Berlin airlift", supplying West Berlin with food and other provisions despite Soviet threats.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200065–70_162-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200065%E2%80%9370-162">[156]</a></sup>

The Soviets mounted a public relations campaign against the policy change. Once again, the East Berlin communists attempted to disrupt the [Berlin municipal elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_Blockade#December_elections "Berlin Blockade") (as they had done in the 1946 elections),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200013_157-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200013-157">[151]</a></sup> which were held on 5 December 1948 and produced a turnout of 86.3% and an overwhelming victory for the non-communist parties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner198729_163-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner198729-163">[157]</a></sup> The results effectively divided the city into East and West, the latter comprising US, British and French sectors. 300,000 Berliners demonstrated and urged the international airlift to continue,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFritsch-Bournazel1990143_164-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFritsch-Bournazel1990143-164">[158]</a></sup> and US Air Force pilot [Gail Halvorsen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gail_Halvorsen "Gail Halvorsen") created "[Operation Vittles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_Blockade#%22Operation_Little_Vittles%22 "Berlin Blockade")", which supplied candy to German children.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200026_165-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200026-165">[159]</a></sup> The Airlift was as much a logistical as a political and psychological success for the West; it firmly linked West Berlin to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaum200811–13,_41_166-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaum200811%E2%80%9313,_41-166">[160]</a></sup> In May 1949, Stalin backed down and lifted the blockade.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200534_96-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200534-96">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller2000180–181_167-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller2000180%E2%80%93181-167">[161]</a></sup>

In 1952, Stalin repeatedly [proposed a plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stalin_Note "Stalin Note") to unify East and West Germany under a single government chosen in elections supervised by the United Nations, if the new Germany were to stay out of Western military alliances, but this proposal was turned down by the Western powers. Some sources dispute the sincerity of the proposal.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEvan_Dijk1996_168-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEvan_Dijk1996-168">[162]</a></sup>

### Beginnings of NATO and Radio Free Europe

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Truman_signing_North_Atlantic_Treaty.jpg/220px-Truman_signing_North_Atlantic_Treaty.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Truman_signing_North_Atlantic_Treaty.jpg)

President Truman signs the [North Atlantic Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty "North Atlantic Treaty") with guests in the Oval Office.

Britain, France, the United States, Canada and eight other western European countries signed the [North Atlantic Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty "North Atlantic Treaty") of April 1949, establishing the [North Atlantic Treaty Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO") (NATO).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200534_96-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200534-96">[90]</a></sup> That August, the [first Soviet atomic device](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RDS-1 "RDS-1") was detonated in [Semipalatinsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semey "Semey"), [Kazakh SSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakh_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194–197_117-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194%E2%80%93197-117">[111]</a></sup> Following Soviet refusals to participate in a German rebuilding effort set forth by western European countries in 1948,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200018_158-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200018-158">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner198723_169-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner198723-169">[163]</a></sup> the US, Britain and France spearheaded the establishment of the [Federal Republic of Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Germany "West Germany") from the [three Western zones of occupation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bizone "Bizone") in April 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBungert1994_170-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBungert1994-170">[164]</a></sup> The Soviet Union proclaimed [its zone of occupation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_occupation_zone_of_Germany "Soviet occupation zone of Germany") in Germany the [German Democratic Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany") that October.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEByrd2003_78-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEByrd2003-78">[72]</a></sup>

Media in the [Eastern Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc") was an [organ of the state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc_media_and_propaganda "Eastern Bloc media and propaganda"), completely reliant on and subservient to the communist party. Radio and television organizations were state-owned, while print media was usually owned by political organizations, mostly by the local communist party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEO'Neil199715–25_171-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Neil199715%E2%80%9325-171">[165]</a></sup> Soviet radio broadcasts used Marxist rhetoric to attack capitalism, emphasizing themes of labor exploitation, imperialism and war-mongering.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWood1992105_172-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWood1992105-172">[166]</a></sup>

Along with the broadcasts of the [BBC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC "BBC") and the [Voice of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voice_of_America "Voice of America") to Central and Eastern Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPuddington2003131_173-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPuddington2003131-173">[167]</a></sup> a major propaganda effort begun in 1949 was [Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe/Radio_Liberty "Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty"), dedicated to bringing about the peaceful demise of the communist system in the Eastern Bloc.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPuddington20039_174-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPuddington20039-174">[168]</a></sup> Radio Free Europe attempted to achieve these goals by serving as a surrogate home radio station, an alternative to the controlled and party-dominated domestic press in the Soviet Bloc.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPuddington20039_174-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPuddington20039-174">[168]</a></sup> Radio Free Europe was a product of some of the most prominent architects of America's early Cold War strategy, especially those who believed that the Cold War would eventually be fought by political rather than military means, such as George F. Kennan.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPuddington20037_175-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPuddington20037-175">[169]</a></sup> Soviet and Eastern Bloc authorities used various methods to suppress Western broadcasts, including [radio jamming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_jamming "Radio jamming").<sup id="cite_ref-Hearings_176-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-Hearings-176">[170]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-177">[171]</a></sup>

American policymakers, including Kennan and [John Foster Dulles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Foster_Dulles "John Foster Dulles"), acknowledged that the Cold War was in its essence a war of ideas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPuddington20037_175-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPuddington20037-175">[169]</a></sup> The United States, acting through the CIA, funded a long list of projects to counter the communist appeal among intellectuals in Europe and the developing world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPuddington200310_178-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPuddington200310-178">[172]</a></sup> The CIA also [covertly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secrecy "Secrecy") sponsored a domestic propaganda campaign called [Crusade for Freedom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crusade_for_Freedom "Crusade for Freedom").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECummings2010_179-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTECummings2010-179">[173]</a></sup>

### German rearmament

The rearmament of West Germany was achieved in the early 1950s. Its main promoter was [Konrad Adenauer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer "Konrad Adenauer"), the chancellor of West Germany, with France the main opponent. Washington had the decisive voice. It was strongly supported by the Pentagon (the US military leadership), and weakly opposed by President Truman; the State Department was ambivalent. The outbreak of the Korean War in June 1950 changed the calculations and Washington now gave full support. That also involved naming [Dwight D. Eisenhower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower "Dwight D. Eisenhower") in charge of NATO forces and sending more American troops to West Germany. There was a strong promise that West Germany would not develop nuclear weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-180"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-180">[174]</a></sup>

Widespread fears of another rise of [German militarism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Militarism#Germany "Militarism") necessitated the new military to operate within an alliance framework under [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO") command.<sup id="cite_ref-181"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-181">[175]</a></sup> In 1955, Washington secured full German membership of NATO.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEByrd2003_78-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEByrd2003-78">[72]</a></sup> In May 1953, [Lavrentiy Beria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lavrentiy_Beria "Lavrentiy Beria"), by then in a government post, had made an unsuccessful proposal to allow the reunification of a neutral Germany to prevent West Germany's incorporation into NATO, but his attempts were cut short after he was [executed several months later](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lavrentiy_Beria#Arrest,_trial_and_execution "Lavrentiy Beria") during a Soviet power struggle.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005105_182-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005105-182">[176]</a></sup> The events led to the establishment of the _[Bundeswehr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bundeswehr "Bundeswehr")_, the West German military, in 1955.<sup id="cite_ref-183"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-183">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-184">[178]</a></sup>

### Chinese Civil War, SEATO, and NSC 68

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Mao%2C_Bulganin%2C_Stalin%2C_Ulbricht_Tsedenbal.jpeg/220px-Mao%2C_Bulganin%2C_Stalin%2C_Ulbricht_Tsedenbal.jpeg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mao,_Bulganin,_Stalin,_Ulbricht_Tsedenbal.jpeg)

[Mao Zedong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mao_Zedong "Mao Zedong") and [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin") in Moscow, December 1949

In 1949, [Mao Zedong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mao_Zedong "Mao Zedong")'s [People's Liberation Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army "People's Liberation Army") defeated [Chiang Kai-shek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek "Chiang Kai-shek")'s United States-backed [Kuomintang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuomintang "Kuomintang") (KMT) Nationalist Government in China. The KMT-controlled territory was now [restricted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuomintang%27s_retreat_to_Taiwan "Kuomintang's retreat to Taiwan") to the island of [Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan"), the nationalist government of which exists to this day. The Kremlin promptly created an alliance with the newly formed People's Republic of China.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200539_185-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200539-185">[179]</a></sup> According to Norwegian historian [Odd Arne Westad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odd_Arne_Westad "Odd Arne Westad"), the communists won the Civil War because they made fewer military mistakes than Chiang Kai-Shek made, and because in his search for a powerful centralized government, Chiang antagonized too many interest groups in China. Moreover, his party was weakened during the [war against Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War "Second Sino-Japanese War"). Meanwhile, the communists told different groups, such as the peasants, exactly what they wanted to hear, and they cloaked themselves under the cover of [Chinese nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_nationalism "Chinese nationalism").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWestad2012291_186-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWestad2012291-186">[180]</a></sup>

Confronted with the [communist revolution in China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Revolution "Chinese Communist Revolution") and [the end of the American atomic monopoly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_atomic_bomb_project "Soviet atomic bomb project") in 1949, the Truman administration quickly moved to escalate and expand its [containment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Containment "Containment") doctrine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194–197_117-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194%E2%80%93197-117">[111]</a></sup> In [NSC 68](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NSC_68 "NSC 68"), a secret 1950 document, the National Security Council proposed reinforcing pro-Western alliance systems and quadrupling spending on defense.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194–197_117-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194%E2%80%93197-117">[111]</a></sup> Truman, under the influence of advisor [Paul Nitze](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Nitze "Paul Nitze"), saw containment as implying complete [rollback](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rollback "Rollback") of Soviet influence in all its forms.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELayne200763–66_187-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELayne200763%E2%80%9366-187">[181]</a></sup>

United States officials moved to expand this version of containment into [Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asia "Asia"), [Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Africa "Africa"), and [Latin America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_America "Latin America"), in order to counter revolutionary nationalist movements, often led by communist parties financed by the USSR.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005212_188-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005212-188">[182]</a></sup> In this way, this US would exercise "[preponderant power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_projection "Power projection")," oppose neutrality, and [establish global](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_strategy "Grand strategy") [hegemony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hegemony "Hegemony").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELayne200763–66_187-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELayne200763%E2%80%9366-187">[181]</a></sup> In the early 1950s (a period sometimes known as the "[Pactomania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pactomania "Pactomania")"), the US formalized a series of alliances with [Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan "Japan") (a former WWII enemy), [South Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Korea "South Korea"), [Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan"), [Australia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia "Australia"), [New Zealand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand "New Zealand"), [Thailand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thailand "Thailand") and the [Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippines "Philippines") (notably [ANZUS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ANZUS "ANZUS") in 1951 and [SEATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Asia_Treaty_Organization "Southeast Asia Treaty Organization") in 1954), thereby guaranteeing the United States a number of long-term military bases.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEByrd2003_78-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEByrd2003-78">[72]</a></sup>

### Korean War

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/IncheonLandingMcArthur.jpg/220px-IncheonLandingMcArthur.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:IncheonLandingMcArthur.jpg)

General [Douglas MacArthur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur "Douglas MacArthur"), UN Command CiC (seated), observes the naval shelling of [Incheon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incheon "Incheon"), Korea from [USS _Mt. McKinley_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USS_Mount_McKinley "USS Mount McKinley"), 15 September 1950.

One of the more significant examples of the implementation of containment was the United Nations US-led intervention in the [Korean War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korean_War "Korean War"). In June 1950, after years of mutual hostilities,<sup id="cite_ref-189"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-189">[G]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHaruki20187–12_190-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHaruki20187%E2%80%9312-190">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStueck2013252–256_191-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStueck2013252%E2%80%93256-191">[184]</a></sup> [Kim Il Sung](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Il_Sung "Kim Il Sung")'s [North Korean People's Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korean_People%27s_Army "Korean People's Army") [invaded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Pokpoong "Operation Pokpoong") [South Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Korea "South Korea") at the [38th parallel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/38th_parallel_north#Korea "38th parallel north"). Stalin had been reluctant to support the invasion<sup id="cite_ref-192"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-192">[H]</a></sup> but ultimately sent advisers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeathersby199328,_30_193-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeathersby199328,_30-193">[185]</a></sup> To Stalin's surprise,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194–197_117-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194%E2%80%93197-117">[111]</a></sup> the [United Nations Security Council Resolution 82](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_82 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 82") and [83](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_83 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 83") backed the defense of South Korea, although the Soviets were then boycotting meetings in protest of the fact that [Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan") (Republic of China), not the [People's Republic of China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China"), held a permanent seat on the council.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMalkasian200116_194-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMalkasian200116-194">[186]</a></sup> A [UN force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Command "United Nations Command") of sixteen countries faced North Korea,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFehrenbach2001305_195-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFehrenbach2001305-195">[187]</a></sup> although 40 percent of troops were South Korean, and about 50 percent were from the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECraigLogevall2012118_196-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraigLogevall2012118-196">[188]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/KoreanWar_recover_Seoul.jpg/220px-KoreanWar_recover_Seoul.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:KoreanWar_recover_Seoul.jpg)

[US Marines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps "United States Marine Corps") engaged in street fighting during the liberation of [Seoul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seoul "Seoul"), September 1950

The US initially seemed to follow containment when it first entered the war. This directed the US's action to only push back North Korea across the 38th Parallel and restore South Korea's sovereignty while allowing North Korea's survival as a state. However, the success of the [Inchon landing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Inchon "Battle of Inchon") inspired the US/UN forces to pursue a [rollback](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rollback "Rollback") strategy instead and to overthrow communist North Korea, thereby allowing nationwide elections under U.N. auspices.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatray1979_197-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatray1979-197">[189]</a></sup> General [Douglas MacArthur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur "Douglas MacArthur") then advanced across the [38th Parallel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Division_of_Korea "Division of Korea") into North Korea. The Chinese, fearful of a possible US invasion, sent in a large army and defeated the U.N. forces, pushing them back below the 38th parallel. Truman publicly hinted that he might use his "ace in the hole" of the atomic bomb, but Mao was unmoved.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatersonCliffordBrighamDonoghue2014286–289_198-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatersonCliffordBrighamDonoghue2014286%E2%80%93289-198">[190]</a></sup> The episode was used to support the wisdom of the containment doctrine as opposed to rollback. The Communists were later pushed to roughly around the original border, with minimal changes. Among other effects, the Korean War galvanised [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO") to develop a military structure.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsbyKamps198513–14_199-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsbyKamps198513%E2%80%9314-199">[191]</a></sup> Public opinion in countries involved, such as Great Britain, was divided for and against the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECotton1989100_200-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTECotton1989100-200">[192]</a></sup>

After the [Korean Armistice Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korean_Armistice_Agreement "Korean Armistice Agreement") was approved in July 1953, North Korean leader [Kim Il Sung](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Il_Sung "Kim Il Sung") created a highly centralized, totalitarian dictatorship that accorded his family unlimited power while generating a pervasive [cult of personality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cult_of_personality "Cult of personality").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOberdorfer200110–11_201-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOberdorfer200110%E2%80%9311-201">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENoOsterholm1996_202-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTENoOsterholm1996-202">[194]</a></sup> In the South, the American-backed dictator [Syngman Rhee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syngman_Rhee "Syngman Rhee") ran an authoritarian regime that engaged in [anti-communist mass killings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-communist_mass_killings "Anti-communist mass killings").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHwang201661–70_203-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHwang201661%E2%80%9370-203">[195]</a></sup> While Rhee was [overthrown in 1960](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/April_Revolution "April Revolution"), South Korea continued to be ruled by a military government of former Japanese collaborators until the re-establishment of a multi-party system in the late 1980s. Subsequently, South Korea experienced an economic boom and became one of the most [advanced countries on the planet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index#Nations "List of countries by Human Development Index").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESuh201325–35_204-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTESuh201325%E2%80%9335-204">[196]</a></sup>

### Khrushchev, Eisenhower, and de-Stalinization

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/1959_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg/220px-1959_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1959_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg)

NATO and Warsaw Pact troop strengths in Europe in 1959

In 1953, changes in political leadership on both sides shifted the dynamic of the Cold War.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916_126-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916-126">[120]</a></sup> [Dwight D. Eisenhower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower "Dwight D. Eisenhower") was inaugurated president that January. During the last 18 months of the Truman administration, the American defense budget had quadrupled, and Eisenhower moved to reduce military spending by a third while continuing to fight the Cold War effectively.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194–197_117-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194%E2%80%93197-117">[111]</a></sup>

Joseph Stalin [died in 1953](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Joseph_Stalin "Death and state funeral of Joseph Stalin"). Without a mutually agreeable successor, the highest Communist Party officials initially opted to rule the Soviet Union jointly through a troika headed by [Georgy Malenkov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgy_Malenkov "Georgy Malenkov"). This did not last, however, and [Nikita Khrushchev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev "Nikita Khrushchev") eventually won the ensuing power struggle by the mid-1950s. In 1956, he [denounced Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/On_the_Cult_of_Personality_and_Its_Consequences "On the Cult of Personality and Its Consequences") and proceeded to ease controls over the party and society. This was known as [de-Stalinization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De-Stalinization "De-Stalinization").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916_126-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916-126">[120]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Voroshilov%2C_Khrushchev%2C_Kekkonen.jpeg/220px-Voroshilov%2C_Khrushchev%2C_Kekkonen.jpeg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Voroshilov,_Khrushchev,_Kekkonen.jpeg)

From left to right: Soviet [head of state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_state "Head of state") [Kliment Voroshilov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kliment_Voroshilov "Kliment Voroshilov"), Soviet premier [Nikita Khrushchev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev "Nikita Khrushchev") and [Finnish president](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Finland "President of Finland") [Urho Kekkonen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urho_Kekkonen "Urho Kekkonen") at Moscow in 1960

On 18 November 1956, while addressing Western dignitaries at a reception in Moscow's Polish embassy, Khrushchev infamously declared, "Whether you like it or not, history is on our side. [We will bury you](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/We_will_bury_you "We will bury you")", shocking everyone present.<sup id="cite_ref-205"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-205">[I]</a></sup> He would later claim he had not been referring to nuclear war, but the "historically fated victory of communism over capitalism."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200584_206-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200584-206">[197]</a></sup> In 1961, Khrushchev boasted that, even if the Soviet Union was currently behind the West, its housing shortage would disappear within ten years, consumer goods would be made abundant, and the "construction of a communist society" would be completed "in the main" within no more than two decades.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETompson1997237–239_207-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTETompson1997237%E2%80%93239-207">[198]</a></sup>

Eisenhower's secretary of state, John Foster Dulles, initiated a "[New Look](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Look_(policy) "New Look (policy)")" for the [containment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Containment "Containment") strategy, calling for a greater reliance on nuclear weapons against US enemies in wartime.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916_126-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916-126">[120]</a></sup> Dulles also enunciated the doctrine of "[massive retaliation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massive_retaliation "Massive retaliation")", threatening a severe US response to any Soviet aggression. Possessing nuclear superiority, for example, allowed Eisenhower to face down Soviet threats to intervene in the Middle East during the 1956 [Suez Crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis "Suez Crisis").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194–197_117-7"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194%E2%80%93197-117">[111]</a></sup> The declassified US plans for retaliatory nuclear strikes in the late 1950s included the "systematic destruction" of 1,200 major urban centers in the Soviet Bloc and China, including Moscow, East Berlin and Beijing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBradner2015_208-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBradner2015-208">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-209">[J]</a></sup>

In spite of these events, there were substantial hopes for détente when [an upswing in diplomacy took place in 1959](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev#Early_relations_and_U.S._visit_(1957%E2%80%931960) "Nikita Khrushchev"), including a two-week visit by Khrushchev to the US, and plans for a two-power summit for May 1960. The latter was disturbed by the [U-2 spy plane scandal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1960_U-2_incident "1960 U-2 incident"), however, in which Eisenhower was caught lying about the intrusion of American surveillance aircraft into Soviet territory.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatersonCliffordBrighamDonoghue2014306–308_210-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatersonCliffordBrighamDonoghue2014306%E2%80%93308-210">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchudson2015_211-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchudson2015-211">[201]</a></sup>

### Warsaw Pact and Hungarian Revolution

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Kossuth_Lajos_utca_a_Ferenciek_tere_fel%C5%91l_n%C3%A9zve._1956._okt%C3%B3ber_25-e_d%C3%A9lut%C3%A1n%2C_-_Fortepan_24652.jpg/220px-Kossuth_Lajos_utca_a_Ferenciek_tere_fel%C5%91l_n%C3%A9zve._1956._okt%C3%B3ber_25-e_d%C3%A9lut%C3%A1n%2C_-_Fortepan_24652.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kossuth_Lajos_utca_a_Ferenciek_tere_fel%C5%91l_n%C3%A9zve._1956._okt%C3%B3ber_25-e_d%C3%A9lut%C3%A1n,_-_Fortepan_24652.jpg)

March of protesters in Budapest, on 25 October;

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg/220px-Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg)

A destroyed Soviet T-34-85 tank in Budapest

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soviet_empire_1960.png/220px-Soviet_empire_1960.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Soviet_empire_1960.png)

The maximum territorial extent of Soviet [influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sphere_of_influence "Sphere of influence"), after the [Cuban Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_Revolution "Cuban Revolution") of 1959 and before the official [Sino-Soviet split](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split "Sino-Soviet split") of 1961

While [Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin")'s death in 1953 slightly relaxed tensions, the situation in Europe remained an uneasy armed truce.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKhanna2013372_212-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKhanna2013372-212">[202]</a></sup> The Soviets, who had already created a network of mutual assistance treaties in the [Eastern Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc") by 1949, established a formal alliance therein, the [Warsaw Pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact "Warsaw Pact"), in 1955. It stood opposed to NATO.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEByrd2003_78-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEByrd2003-78">[72]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Hole_in_flag_-_Budapest_1956.jpg/170px-Hole_in_flag_-_Budapest_1956.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Hole_in_flag_-_Budapest_1956.jpg)

[Hungarian flag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_of_Hungary "Flag of Hungary") (1949–1956) with the communist coat of arms cut out was an anti-Soviet revolutionary symbol

The [Hungarian Revolution of 1956](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1956 "Hungarian Revolution of 1956") occurred shortly after Khrushchev arranged the removal of Hungary's Stalinist leader [Mátyás Rákosi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M%C3%A1ty%C3%A1s_R%C3%A1kosi "Mátyás Rákosi").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC1956_213-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC1956-213">[203]</a></sup> In response to a popular anti-communist uprising,<sup id="cite_ref-214"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-214">[K]</a></sup> the new regime formally disbanded the [secret police](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_Protection_Authority "State Protection Authority"), declared its intention to withdraw from the Warsaw Pact and pledged to re-establish free elections. The [Soviet Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Army "Soviet Army") invaded.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUN_General_Assembly1957_215-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUN_General_Assembly1957-215">[204]</a></sup> Thousands of Hungarians were killed and arrested, imprisoned and deported to the Soviet Union,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolodkov1956_216-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolodkov1956-216">[205]</a></sup> and approximately 200,000 Hungarians fled Hungary in the chaos.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECseresnyés199986–101_217-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTECseresny%C3%A9s199986%E2%80%93101-217">[206]</a></sup> Hungarian leader [Imre Nagy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imre_Nagy "Imre Nagy") and others were executed following secret trials.<sup id="cite_ref-218"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-218">[L]</a></sup>

From 1957 through 1961, Khrushchev openly and repeatedly threatened the West with nuclear annihilation. He claimed that Soviet missile capabilities were far superior to those of the United States, capable of wiping out any American or European city. According to [John Lewis Gaddis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Lewis_Gaddis "John Lewis Gaddis"), Khrushchev rejected Stalin's "belief in the inevitability of war," however. The new leader declared his ultimate goal was "[peaceful coexistence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peaceful_coexistence "Peaceful coexistence")".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200570_219-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200570-219">[207]</a></sup> In Khrushchev's formulation, peace would allow capitalism to collapse on its own,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerlmutter1997145_220-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerlmutter1997145-220">[208]</a></sup> as well as giving the Soviets time to boost their military capabilities,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENjølstad2004136_221-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTENj%C3%B8lstad2004136-221">[209]</a></sup> which remained for decades until Gorbachev's later "new thinking" envisioning peaceful coexistence as an end in itself rather than a form of class struggle.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBreslauer200272_222-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBreslauer200272-222">[210]</a></sup>

The events in Hungary produced ideological fractures within the communist parties of the world, particularly in Western Europe, with great decline in membership, as many in both western and socialist countries felt disillusioned by the brutal Soviet response.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELendvai2008196_223-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELendvai2008196-223">[211]</a></sup> The communist parties in the West would never recover from the effect the Hungarian Revolution had on their membership, a fact that was immediately recognized by some, such as the Yugoslavian politician [Milovan Đilas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milovan_Djilas "Milovan Djilas") who shortly after the revolution was crushed said that "The wound which the Hungarian Revolution inflicted on communism can never be completely healed".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELendvai2008196_223-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELendvai2008196-223">[211]</a></sup>

### Rapacki Plan and Berlin Crisis of 1958–1959

In 1957, Polish foreign minister [Adam Rapacki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adam_Rapacki "Adam Rapacki") proposed the [Rapacki Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapacki_Plan "Rapacki Plan") for a nuclear free zone in central Europe. Public opinion tended to be favourable in the West, but it was rejected by leaders of West Germany, Britain, France and the United States. They feared it would leave the powerful conventional armies of the Warsaw Pact dominant over the weaker NATO armies.<sup id="cite_ref-224"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-224">[212]</a></sup>

During November 1958, Khrushchev made an unsuccessful attempt to turn all of Berlin into an independent, demilitarized "free city". He gave the United States, Great Britain and France a six-month ultimatum to withdraw their troops from the sectors of West Berlin, or he would transfer control of Western access rights to the East Germans. Khrushchev earlier explained to [Mao Zedong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mao_Zedong "Mao Zedong") that "Berlin is the testicles of the West. Every time I want to make the West scream, I squeeze on Berlin."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200571_225-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200571-225">[213]</a></sup> NATO formally rejected the ultimatum in mid-December and Khrushchev withdrew it in return for a Geneva conference on the German question.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaubman2004488–502_226-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaubman2004488%E2%80%93502-226">[214]</a></sup>

### American military buildup

[John F. Kennedy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_F._Kennedy "John F. Kennedy")'s foreign policy was dominated by American confrontations with the Soviet Union, manifested by proxy contests. Like Truman and Eisenhower, Kennedy supported containment to stop the spread of Communism. President Eisenhower's [New Look](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Look_(policy) "New Look (policy)") policy had emphasized the use of less expensive nuclear weapons to [deter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deterrence_theory "Deterrence theory") Soviet aggression by threatening massive nuclear attacks on all of the Soviet Union. Nuclear weapons were much cheaper than maintaining a large standing army, so Eisenhower cut conventional forces to save money. Kennedy implemented a new strategy known as [flexible response](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flexible_response "Flexible response"). This strategy relied on conventional arms to achieve limited goals. As part of this policy, Kennedy expanded the [United States special operations forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_special_operations_forces "United States special operations forces"), elite military units that could fight unconventionally in various conflicts. Kennedy hoped that the flexible response strategy would allow the US to counter Soviet influence without resorting to nuclear war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008704–705_227-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008704%E2%80%93705-227">[215]</a></sup>

To support his new strategy, Kennedy ordered a massive increase in defense spending. He sought, and Congress provided, a rapid build-up of the nuclear arsenal to restore the lost superiority over the Soviet Union—he claimed in 1960 that Eisenhower had lost it because of excessive concern with budget deficits. In his inaugural address, Kennedy promised "to bear any burden" in the defense of liberty, and he repeatedly asked for increases in military spending and authorization of new weapons systems. From 1961 to 1964, the number of nuclear weapons increased by 50 percent, as did the number of B-52 bombers to deliver them. The new ICBM force grew from 63 intercontinental ballistic missiles to 424. He authorized 23 new Polaris submarines, each of which carried 16 nuclear missiles. Kennedy also called on cities to construct fallout shelters.<sup id="cite_ref-228"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-228">[216]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-229">[217]</a></sup>

### Competition in the Third World

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonization_1945.png/440px-Colonization_1945.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Colonization_1945.png)

European [colonial empires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_empire "Colonial empire") in Asia and Africa all collapsed in the years after 1945.

Nationalist movements in some countries and regions, notably [Guatemala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guatemala "Guatemala"), Indonesia and [Indochina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainland_Southeast_Asia "Mainland Southeast Asia"), were often allied with communist groups or otherwise perceived to be unfriendly to Western interests.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916_126-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916-126">[120]</a></sup> In this context, the United States and the Soviet Union increasingly competed for influence by proxy in the Third World as [decolonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decolonization "Decolonization") gained momentum in the 1950s and early 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005121–124_230-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005121%E2%80%93124-230">[218]</a></sup> Both sides were selling armaments to gain influence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETowle2000160_231-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTETowle2000160-231">[219]</a></sup> The Kremlin saw continuing territorial losses by imperial powers as presaging the eventual victory of their ideology.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETucker20101566_232-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTETucker20101566-232">[220]</a></sup>

The United States used the [Central Intelligence Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency "Central Intelligence Agency") (CIA) to undermine neutral or hostile Third World governments and to support allied ones.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarabell199964,_916_233-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarabell199964,_916-233">[221]</a></sup> In 1953, President Eisenhower implemented [Operation Ajax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1953_Iranian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat#Execution_of_Operation_Ajax "1953 Iranian coup d'état"), a covert coup operation to overthrow the Iranian prime minister, [Mohammad Mosaddegh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Mosaddegh "Mohammad Mosaddegh"). The popularly elected Mosaddegh had been a Middle Eastern nemesis of Britain since nationalizing the British-owned [Anglo-Iranian Oil Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Persian_Oil_Company "Anglo-Persian Oil Company") in 1951. [Winston Churchill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill") told the United States that Mosaddegh was "increasingly turning towards Communist influence."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGasiorowskiByrne2004125_234-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGasiorowskiByrne2004125-234">[222]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith1953_235-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith1953-235">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorge_Washington_University1953_236-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorge_Washington_University1953-236">[224]</a></sup> The pro-Western [shah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shah "Shah"), [Mohammad Reza Pahlavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi "Mohammad Reza Pahlavi"), assumed control as an [autocratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autocracy "Autocracy") monarch.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWatson2002118_237-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatson2002118-237">[225]</a></sup> The shah's policies included banning the communist [Tudeh Party of Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tudeh_Party_of_Iran "Tudeh Party of Iran"), and general suppression of political dissent by [SAVAK](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SAVAK "SAVAK"), the shah's domestic security and intelligence agency.

In Guatemala, a [banana republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banana_republic "Banana republic"), the [1954 Guatemalan coup d'état](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1954_Guatemalan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1954 Guatemalan coup d'état") ousted the left-wing President [Jacobo Árbenz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacobo_%C3%81rbenz "Jacobo Árbenz") with material CIA support.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStone2010199,_256_238-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStone2010199,_256-238">[226]</a></sup> The post-Arbenz government—a [military junta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_dictatorship "Military dictatorship") headed by [Carlos Castillo Armas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carlos_Castillo_Armas "Carlos Castillo Armas")—repealed a [progressive land reform law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decree_900 "Decree 900"), returned nationalized property belonging to the [United Fruit Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Fruit_Company "United Fruit Company"), set up a [National Committee of Defense Against Communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Committee_of_Defense_Against_Communism "National Committee of Defense Against Communism"), and decreed a [Preventive Penal Law Against Communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Preventive_Penal_Law_Against_Communism "Preventive Penal Law Against Communism") at the request of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulmer-Thomas1987142_239-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulmer-Thomas1987142-239">[227]</a></sup>

The non-aligned Indonesian government of [Sukarno](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sukarno "Sukarno") was faced with a major threat to its legitimacy beginning in 1956 when several regional commanders began to demand autonomy from [Jakarta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jakarta "Jakarta").
