After mediation failed, Sukarno took action to remove the dissident commanders. In February 1958, dissident military commanders in Central Sumatra (Colonel [Ahmad Husein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_Husein "Ahmad Husein")) and North Sulawesi (Colonel Ventje Sumual) declared the [Revolutionary Government of the Republic of Indonesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutionary_Government_of_the_Republic_of_Indonesia "Revolutionary Government of the Republic of Indonesia")\-[Permesta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permesta "Permesta") Movement aimed at overthrowing the Sukarno regime. They were joined by many civilian politicians from the [Masyumi Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masyumi_Party "Masyumi Party"), such as [Sjafruddin Prawiranegara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sjafruddin_Prawiranegara "Sjafruddin Prawiranegara"), who were opposed to the growing influence of the communist [Partai Komunis Indonesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Indonesia "Communist Party of Indonesia"). Due to their anti-communist rhetoric, the rebels received arms, funding, and other covert aid from the CIA until [Allen Lawrence Pope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allen_Lawrence_Pope "Allen Lawrence Pope"), an American pilot, was shot down after a bombing raid on government-held [Ambon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ambon,_Maluku "Ambon, Maluku") in April 1958. The central government responded by launching airborne and seaborne military invasions of rebel strongholds at [Padang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Padang "Padang") and [Manado](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manado "Manado"). By the end of 1958, the rebels were militarily defeated, and the last remaining rebel guerilla bands surrendered by August 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoadnight2002_240-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoadnight2002-240">[228]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/The_Soviet_Union_1961_CPA_2576_stamp_%28The_Struggle_for_the_Liberation_of_Africa._Lumumba_%28_1925-1961_%29%2C_premier_of_Congo%29.jpg/170px-The_Soviet_Union_1961_CPA_2576_stamp_%28The_Struggle_for_the_Liberation_of_Africa._Lumumba_%28_1925-1961_%29%2C_premier_of_Congo%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Soviet_Union_1961_CPA_2576_stamp_(The_Struggle_for_the_Liberation_of_Africa._Lumumba_(_1925-1961_),_premier_of_Congo).jpg)

1961 Russian stamp commemorating [Patrice Lumumba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba "Patrice Lumumba"), assassinated prime minister of the [Republic of the Congo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville) "Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)")

In the [Republic of the Congo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville) "Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)"), also known as Congo-Léopoldville, newly independent from [Belgium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belgium "Belgium") since June 1960, the [Congo Crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congo_Crisis "Congo Crisis") erupted on 5 July leading to the secession of the regions [Katanga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_of_Katanga "State of Katanga") and [South Kasai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Kasai "South Kasai"). CIA-backed President [Joseph Kasa-Vubu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu "Joseph Kasa-Vubu") ordered the dismissal of the democratically elected Prime Minister [Patrice Lumumba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba "Patrice Lumumba") and the Lumumba cabinet in September over massacres by the armed forces during the [invasion of South Kasai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invasion_of_South_Kasai "Invasion of South Kasai") and for involving Soviets in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENzongola-Ntalaja2011108_241-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTENzongola-Ntalaja2011108-241">[229]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchraeder199457_242-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchraeder199457-242">[230]</a></sup> Later the CIA-backed Colonel [Mobutu Sese Seko](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko "Mobutu Sese Seko") quickly mobilized his forces to seize power through a military coup d'état, <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchraeder199457_242-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchraeder199457-242">[230]</a></sup> and worked with Western intelligence agencies to imprison Lumumba and hand him over to Katangan authorities who executed him by firing squad.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENzongola-Ntalaja2011_243-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTENzongola-Ntalaja2011-243">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGerard2015216–218_244-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGerard2015216%E2%80%93218-244">[232]</a></sup>

In [British Guiana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Guiana "British Guiana"), the leftist [People's Progressive Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Progressive_Party/Civic "People's Progressive Party/Civic") (PPP) candidate [Cheddi Jagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cheddi_Jagan "Cheddi Jagan") won the position of chief minister in a colonially administered election in 1953 but was quickly forced to resign from power after Britain's suspension of the still-dependent nation's constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERose200257_245-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERose200257-245">[233]</a></sup> Embarrassed by the landslide electoral victory of Jagan's allegedly Marxist party, the British imprisoned the PPP's leadership and maneuvered the organization into a divisive rupture in 1955, engineering a split between Jagan and his PPP colleagues.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsYoung2004xviii_246-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsYoung2004xviii-246">[234]</a></sup> Jagan again won the colonial elections in 1957 and 1961, despite Britain's shift to a reconsideration of its view of the left-wing Jagan as a Soviet-style communist at this time. The United States pressured the British to withhold [Guyana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guyana "Guyana")'s independence until an alternative to Jagan could be identified, supported, and brought into office.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer2010247–248_247-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer2010247%E2%80%93248-247">[235]</a></sup>

Worn down by the [communist guerrilla war for Vietnamese independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Indochina_War "First Indochina War") and handed a watershed defeat by communist [Viet Minh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viet_Minh "Viet Minh") rebels at the 1954 [Battle of Dien Bien Phu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Dien_Bien_Phu "Battle of Dien Bien Phu"), the French accepted a negotiated abandonment of their colonial stake in [Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam "Vietnam"). In the [Geneva Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1954_Geneva_Conference "1954 Geneva Conference"), peace accords were signed, leaving Vietnam divided between a pro-Soviet administration in [North Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Vietnam "North Vietnam") and a pro-Western administration in [South Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Vietnam "South Vietnam") at the [17th parallel north](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/17th_parallel_north "17th parallel north"). Between 1954 and 1961, Eisenhower's United States sent economic aid and military advisers to strengthen South Vietnam's pro-Western government against communist efforts to destabilize it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194–197_117-8"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194%E2%80%93197-117">[111]</a></sup>

Many emerging nations of Asia, Africa, and Latin America rejected the pressure to choose sides in the East–West competition. In 1955, at the [Bandung Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandung_Conference "Bandung Conference") in Indonesia, dozens of Third World governments resolved to stay out of the Cold War.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005126_248-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005126-248">[236]</a></sup> The consensus reached at Bandung culminated with the creation of the [Belgrade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belgrade "Belgrade")\-headquartered [Non-Aligned Movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement "Non-Aligned Movement") in 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916_126-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916-126">[120]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Khrushchev broadened Moscow's policy to establish ties with [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India "India") and other key neutral states. Independence movements in the Third World transformed the post-war order into a more pluralistic world of decolonized African and Middle Eastern nations and of rising nationalism in Asia and Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194–197_117-9"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194%E2%80%93197-117">[111]</a></sup>

### Sino-Soviet split

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soviet_empire_1960.png/220px-Soviet_empire_1960.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Soviet_empire_1960.png)

Map showing greatest territorial extent of the Soviet Union and the states that it dominated politically, economically and militarily in 1960, after the [Cuban Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_Revolution "Cuban Revolution") of 1959 but before the official [Sino-Soviet split](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split "Sino-Soviet split") of 1961 (total area: c. 35,000,000 km<sup>2</sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-249"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-249">[M]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Sino-Soviet_split_1980.svg/280px-Sino-Soviet_split_1980.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sino-Soviet_split_1980.svg)

A map showing the relations of [Marxist–Leninist states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_state "Communist state") after the Sino-Soviet split of 1980:

  The USSR and pro-Soviet socialist states

  China and pro-Chinese socialist states

  Non-socialist states

After 1956, the Sino-Soviet alliance began to break down. Mao had defended Stalin when Khrushchev criticized him in 1956 and treated the new Soviet leader as a superficial upstart, accusing him of having lost his revolutionary edge.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005142_250-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005142-250">[237]</a></sup> For his part, Khrushchev, disturbed by Mao's glib attitude toward nuclear war, referred to the Chinese leader as a "lunatic on a throne".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKempe201142_251-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKempe201142-251">[238]</a></sup>

After this, Khrushchev made many desperate attempts to reconstitute the Sino-Soviet alliance, but Mao considered it useless and denied any proposal.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005142_250-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005142-250">[237]</a></sup> The Chinese-Soviet animosity spilled out in an intra-communist propaganda war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELüthi2010273–276_252-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEL%C3%BCthi2010273%E2%80%93276-252">[239]</a></sup> Further on, the Soviets focused on a bitter rivalry with Mao's China for leadership of the global communist movement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005140–142_253-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005140%E2%80%93142-253">[240]</a></sup> Historian Lorenz M. Lüthi argues:

The Sino-Soviet split was one of the key events of the Cold War, equal in importance to the construction of the Berlin Wall, the Cuban Missile Crisis, the Second Vietnam War, and [Sino-American rapprochement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China%E2%80%93United_States_relations#Rapprochement "China–United States relations"). The split helped to determine the framework of the [Second Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Cold_War "Second Cold War") in general, and influenced the course of the Second Vietnam War in particular.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELüthi20101_254-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEL%C3%BCthi20101-254">[241]</a></sup>

### Space Race

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag.jpg/200px-Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag.jpg)

The United States [reached the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11 "Apollo 11") in 1969.

On the [nuclear weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon "Nuclear weapon") front, the United States and the Soviet Union pursued nuclear rearmament and developed long-range weapons with which they could strike the territory of the other.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEByrd2003_78-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEByrd2003-78">[72]</a></sup> In August 1957, the Soviets successfully launched the world's first [intercontinental ballistic missile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intercontinental_ballistic_missile "Intercontinental ballistic missile") (ICBM),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcMahon200375–76_255-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcMahon200375%E2%80%9376-255">[242]</a></sup> and in October they launched the first Earth satellite, [Sputnik 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sputnik_1 "Sputnik 1").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC1957_256-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC1957-256">[243]</a></sup> The launch of Sputnik inaugurated the [Space Race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Race "Space Race"). This led to the [Apollo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_program "Apollo program") [Moon landings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_landing "Moon landing") by the United States, which astronaut [Frank Borman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Borman "Frank Borman") later described as "just a battle in the Cold War."<sup id="cite_ref-257"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-257">[244]</a></sup> The public's reaction in the Soviet Union was mixed. The Soviet government limited the release of information about the lunar landing, which affected the reaction. A portion of the populace did not give it any attention, and another portion was angered by it.<sup id="cite_ref-258"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-258">[245]</a></sup> A major Cold War element of the Space Race was [satellite reconnaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconnaissance_satellite "Reconnaissance satellite"), as well as signals intelligence to gauge which aspects of the space programs had military capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-259"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-259">[246]</a></sup>

Later, however, the US and USSR pursued some cooperation in space as part of [détente](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D%C3%A9tente "Détente"), such as [Apollo–Soyuz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz "Apollo–Soyuz").<sup id="cite_ref-260"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-260">[247]</a></sup>

### Aftermath of the Cuban Revolution

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/170px-CheyFidel.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CheyFidel.jpg)

[Che Guevara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara "Che Guevara") (left) and [Fidel Castro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro "Fidel Castro") (right) in 1961

In [Cuba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuba "Cuba"), the [26th of July Movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/26th_of_July_Movement "26th of July Movement"), led by young revolutionaries [Fidel Castro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro "Fidel Castro") and [Che Guevara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara "Che Guevara"), seized power in the [Cuban Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_Revolution "Cuban Revolution") on 1 January 1959, toppling President [Fulgencio Batista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fulgencio_Batista "Fulgencio Batista"), whose unpopular regime had been denied arms by the Eisenhower administration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlumberg199523–24_261-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlumberg199523%E2%80%9324-261">[248]</a></sup> Although Fidel Castro's first refused to categorize his new government as socialist and repeatedly denying being a communist, Castro appointed Marxists to senior government and military positions. Most significantly, Che Guevara became Governor of the Central Bank and then Minister of Industries.<sup id="cite_ref-262"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-262">[249]</a></sup>

[Diplomatic relations between Cuba and the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuba%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Cuba–United States relations") continued for some time after Batista's fall, but President Eisenhower deliberately left the capital to avoid meeting Castro during the latter's trip to [Washington, D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C.") in April, leaving Vice President [Richard Nixon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Nixon "Richard Nixon") to conduct the meeting in his place.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELechuga_Hevia2001142_263-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELechuga_Hevia2001142-263">[250]</a></sup> Cuba began negotiating for arms purchases from the Eastern Bloc in March 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDominguez198922_264-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDominguez198922-264">[251]</a></sup> The same month, Eisenhower gave approval to [CIA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency "Central Intelligence Agency") plans and funding to overthrow Castro.<sup id="cite_ref-265"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-265">[252]</a></sup>

In January 1961, just prior to leaving office, Eisenhower formally severed relations with the Cuban government. That April, the administration of newly elected American President [John F. Kennedy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_F._Kennedy "John F. Kennedy") mounted the unsuccessful CIA-organized [ship-borne invasion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion "Bay of Pigs Invasion") of the island by [Cuban exiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_exodus "Cuban exodus") at Playa Girón and Playa Larga in [Santa Clara Province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santa_Clara_Province "Santa Clara Province")—a failure that publicly humiliated the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith199895_266-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith199895-266">[253]</a></sup> Castro responded by publicly embracing [Marxism–Leninism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism "Marxism–Leninism"), and the Soviet Union pledged to [provide further support](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuba%E2%80%93Soviet_Union_relations "Cuba–Soviet Union relations").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith199895_266-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith199895-266">[253]</a></sup> In December, the US government [began a violent campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Mongoose "Operation Mongoose") of [terrorist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terrorism "Terrorism") attacks against civilians in Cuba, and [covert operations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Covert_operations "Covert operations") and sabotage against the administration, in an attempt to overthrow the Cuban government.<sup id="cite_ref-273"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-273">[260]</a></sup>

### Berlin Crisis of 1961

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/US_Army_tanks_face_off_against_Soviet_tanks%2C_Berlin_1961.jpg/220px-US_Army_tanks_face_off_against_Soviet_tanks%2C_Berlin_1961.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:US_Army_tanks_face_off_against_Soviet_tanks,_Berlin_1961.jpg)

[Soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanks_of_the_Soviet_Union "Tanks of the Soviet Union") and [American tanks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanks_of_the_United_States "Tanks of the United States") face each other at [Checkpoint Charlie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Checkpoint_Charlie "Checkpoint Charlie") during the Berlin Crisis of 1961

The [Berlin Crisis of 1961](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_Crisis_of_1961 "Berlin Crisis of 1961") was the last major incident in the Cold War regarding the status of Berlin and [post–World War II Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Germany_(1945%E2%80%931990) "History of Germany (1945–1990)"). By the early 1950s, the [Soviet approach to restricting emigration movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emigration_from_the_Eastern_Bloc "Emigration from the Eastern Bloc") was emulated by most of the rest of the [Eastern Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDowty1989114_274-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDowty1989114-274">[261]</a></sup> However, hundreds of thousands of [East Germans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany") annually emigrated to free and prosperous [West Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Germany "West Germany") through a "loophole" in the system that existed between [East Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Berlin "East Berlin") and [West Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Berlin "West Berlin").<sup id="cite_ref-275"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-275">[262]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison200399_276-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison200399-276">[263]</a></sup>

The emigration resulted in a massive "[brain drain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_capital_flight "Human capital flight")" from East Germany to West Germany of younger educated professionals, such that nearly 20% of East Germany's population had migrated to West Germany by 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDowty1989122_277-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDowty1989122-277">[264]</a></sup> That June, the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") issued a new [ultimatum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultimatum "Ultimatum") demanding the withdrawal of [Allied forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II") from West Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005114_278-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005114-278">[265]</a></sup> The request was rebuffed, but the United States now limited its security guarantees to West Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaum200827_279-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaum200827-279">[266]</a></sup> On 13 August, East Germany erected a barbed-wire barrier that would eventually be expanded through construction into the [Berlin Wall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_Wall "Berlin Wall"), effectively closing the loophole and preventing its citizens from fleeing to the West.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPearson199875_280-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPearson199875-280">[267]</a></sup>

### Cuban Missile Crisis and Khrushchev's ousting

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Cuban_missiles.jpg/220px-Cuban_missiles.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cuban_missiles.jpg)

Aerial photograph of a Soviet missile site in [Cuba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuba "Cuba"), taken by a US [spy aircraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surveillance_aircraft "Surveillance aircraft"), 1 November 1962

The Kennedy administration continued seeking ways to oust Castro following the Bay of Pigs invasion, experimenting with various ways of covertly facilitating the overthrow of the Cuban government. Significant hopes were pinned on the program of terrorist attacks and other destabilization operations known as [Operation Mongoose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Mongoose "Operation Mongoose"), that was devised under the Kennedy administration in 1961. Khrushchev learned of the project in February 1962,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZubok1994_281-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZubok1994-281">[268]</a></sup> and preparations to install Soviet nuclear missiles in Cuba were undertaken in response.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZubok1994_281-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZubok1994-281">[268]</a></sup>

Alarmed, Kennedy considered various reactions. He ultimately responded to the installation of nuclear missiles in Cuba with a [naval blockade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naval_blockade "Naval blockade"), and he presented an ultimatum to the Soviets. Khrushchev backed down from a confrontation, and the Soviet Union removed the missiles in return for a public American pledge not to invade Cuba again as well as a covert deal to remove US missiles from Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH._Jones2009122_282-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH._Jones2009122-282">[269]</a></sup> Castro later admitted that "I would have agreed to the use of nuclear weapons. ... we took it for granted that it would become a nuclear war anyway, and that we were going to disappear."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlightAllynWelch2002252_283-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlightAllynWelch2002252-283">[270]</a></sup>

The [Cuban Missile Crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis "Cuban Missile Crisis") (October–November 1962) brought the world closer to [nuclear war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_warfare "Nuclear warfare") than ever before.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis200582_284-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis200582-284">[271]</a></sup> The aftermath led to efforts in the [nuclear arms race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_arms_race "Nuclear arms race") at nuclear disarmament and improving relations, although the Cold War's first arms control agreement, the [Antarctic Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antarctic_Treaty_System "Antarctic Treaty System"), had come into force in 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-285"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-285">[N]</a></sup>

The compromise embarrassed Khrushchev and the Soviet Union because the withdrawal of US missiles from Italy and Turkey was a secret deal between Kennedy and Khrushchev, and the Soviets were seen as retreating from circumstances that they had started. In 1964, Khrushchev's Kremlin colleagues managed to [oust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev#Removal "Nikita Khrushchev") him, but allowed him a peaceful retirement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005119–120_286-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005119%E2%80%93120-286">[272]</a></sup> He was accused of rudeness and incompetence, and John Lewis Gaddis argues that he was also blamed with ruining Soviet agriculture, bringing the world to the brink of nuclear war, and becoming an "international embarrassment" when he authorized construction of the Berlin Wall.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005119_287-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005119-287">[273]</a></sup> According to Dobrynin, the top Soviet leadership took the Cuban outcome as "a blow to its prestige bordering on humiliation".<sup id="cite_ref-288"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-288">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Malin_Notes_289-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-The_Malin_Notes-289">[275]</a></sup>

## From confrontation to détente (1962–1979)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Glassboro-meeting1967.jpg/250px-Glassboro-meeting1967.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Glassboro-meeting1967.jpg)

Soviet Premier [Alexei Kosygin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexei_Kosygin "Alexei Kosygin") with U.S. President [Lyndon B. Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson "Lyndon B. Johnson") at the 1967 [Glassboro Summit Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glassboro_Summit_Conference "Glassboro Summit Conference").

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/1973_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg/220px-1973_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1973_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg)

NATO and Warsaw Pact troop strengths in Europe in 1973

In the course of the 1960s and 1970s, Cold War participants struggled to adjust to a new, more complicated pattern of international relations in which the world was no longer divided into two clearly opposed blocs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916_126-7"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916-126">[120]</a></sup> From the beginning of the post-war period, with American help Western Europe and Japan rapidly recovered from the destruction of World War II and sustained strong economic growth through the 1950s and 1960s, with per capita GDPs approaching those of the United States, while [Eastern Bloc economies stagnated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc#Economies "Eastern Bloc").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916_126-8"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916-126">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHardtKaufman199516_290-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHardtKaufman199516-290">[276]</a></sup>

The [Vietnam War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam_War "Vietnam War") descended into a quagmire for the United States, leading to a decline in international prestige and economic stability, derailing arms agreements, and provoking domestic unrest. America's withdrawal from the war led it to embrace a policy of [détente](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D%C3%A9tente "Détente") with both China and the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMilestones:_1969–1976_291-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilestones:_1969%E2%80%931976-291">[277]</a></sup>

In the [1973 oil crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_oil_crisis "1973 oil crisis"), Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries ([OPEC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OPEC "OPEC")) cut their petroleum output. This raised oil prices and hurt Western economies, but helped the Soviet Union by generating a huge flow of money from its oil sales.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPainter2014_292-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPainter2014-292">[278]</a></sup>

As a result of the oil crisis, combined with the growing influence of Third World alignments such as OPEC and the [Non-Aligned Movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement "Non-Aligned Movement"), less powerful countries had more room to assert their independence and often showed themselves resistant to pressure from either superpower.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005212_188-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005212-188">[182]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Moscow was forced to turn its attention inward to deal with the Soviet Union's deep-seated domestic economic problems.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916_126-9"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916-126">[120]</a></sup> During this period, Soviet leaders such as [Leonid Brezhnev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev "Leonid Brezhnev") and [Alexei Kosygin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexei_Kosygin "Alexei Kosygin") embraced the notion of détente.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916_126-10"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarabell1999916-126">[120]</a></sup>

### Vietnam War

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Bruce_Crandall%27s_UH-1D.jpg/220px-Bruce_Crandall%27s_UH-1D.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bruce_Crandall%27s_UH-1D.jpg)

US combat operations during the [Battle of Ia Drang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Ia_Drang "Battle of Ia Drang"), [South Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Vietnam "South Vietnam"), November 1965

Under President [John F. Kennedy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_F._Kennedy "John F. Kennedy"), US troop levels in Vietnam grew under the [Military Assistance Advisory Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_Assistance_Advisory_Group "Military Assistance Advisory Group") program from just under a thousand in 1959 to 16,000 in 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-293"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-293">[O]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-294"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-294">[P]</a></sup> South Vietnamese President Ngo Dinh Diem's heavy-handed [crackdown on Buddhist monks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hu%E1%BA%BF_Ph%E1%BA%ADt_%C4%90%E1%BA%A3n_shootings "Huế Phật Đản shootings") in 1963 led the US to endorse a deadly [military coup against Diem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1963_South_Vietnamese_coup "1963 South Vietnamese coup").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMillerWainstock2013315–325_295-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMillerWainstock2013315%E2%80%93325-295">[279]</a></sup> The war escalated further in 1964 following the controversial [Gulf of Tonkin incident](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Tonkin_incident "Gulf of Tonkin incident"), in which a US destroyer was alleged to have clashed with North Vietnamese fast attack craft. The [Gulf of Tonkin Resolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Tonkin_Resolution "Gulf of Tonkin Resolution") gave President [Lyndon B. Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson "Lyndon B. Johnson") broad authorization to increase US military presence, deploying ground [combat units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_organization "Military organization") for the first time and increasing troop levels to 184,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKoven201593_296-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKoven201593-296">[280]</a></sup> Soviet leader Leonid Brezhnev responded by reversing Khrushchev's policy of disengagement and increasing aid to the North Vietnamese, hoping to entice the North from its pro-Chinese position. The USSR discouraged further escalation of the war, however, providing just enough military assistance to tie up American forces.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETucker2011131_297-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTETucker2011131-297">[281]</a></sup> From this point, the [People's Army of Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Army_of_Vietnam "People's Army of Vietnam") (PAVN), also known as the North Vietnamese Army (NVA), engaged in more [conventional warfare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conventional_warfare "Conventional warfare") with US and South Vietnamese forces.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGlass2017_298-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlass2017-298">[282]</a></sup>

The [Tet Offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tet_Offensive "Tet Offensive") of 1968 proved to be the turning point of the war. Despite years of American tutelage and aid, the South Vietnamese forces were unable to withstand the communist offensive and the task fell to US forces instead. Tet showed that the end of US involvement was not in sight, increasing domestic skepticism of the war and giving rise to what was referred to as the [Vietnam Syndrome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam_Syndrome "Vietnam Syndrome"), a public aversion to American overseas military involvements. Nonetheless, operations continued to cross international boundaries: bordering areas of Laos and Cambodia were used by North Vietnam as [supply routes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_trail "Ho Chi Minh trail"), and were heavily [bombed by US forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Barrel_Roll "Operation Barrel Roll").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKalb2013_299-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKalb2013-299">[283]</a></sup>

At the same time, in 1963–1965, American domestic politics saw the triumph of [liberalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States "Modern liberalism in the United States"). According to historian Joseph Crespino:

It has become a staple of twentieth-century historiography that Cold War concerns were at the root of a number of progressive political accomplishments in the postwar period: a high progressive marginal tax rate that helped fund the arms race and contributed to broad income equality; bipartisan support for far-reaching civil rights legislation that transformed politics and society in the American South, which had long given the lie to America's egalitarian ethos; bipartisan support for overturning an explicitly racist immigration system that had been in place since the 1920s; and free health care for the elderly and the poor, a partial fulfillment of one of the unaccomplished goals of the New Deal era. The list could go on.<sup id="cite_ref-300"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-300">[284]</a></sup>

### French withdrawal from NATO military structures

The unity of NATO was breached early in its history, with a crisis occurring during [Charles de Gaulle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle "Charles de Gaulle")'s presidency of France. De Gaulle protested at the strong role of the United States in the organization and what he perceived as a [special relationship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Relationship "Special Relationship") between the United States and the United Kingdom. In a memorandum sent to President [Dwight D. Eisenhower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower "Dwight D. Eisenhower") and Prime Minister [Harold Macmillan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harold_Macmillan "Harold Macmillan") on 17 September 1958, he argued for the creation of a tripartite directorate that would put France on an equal footing with the United States and the United Kingdom, and also for the expansion of NATO's coverage to include geographical areas of interest to France, most notably [French Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Algeria "French Algeria"), where France was waging a counter-insurgency and sought NATO assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMenon200011_301-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMenon200011-301">[285]</a></sup> De Gaulle considered the response he received to be unsatisfactory and began the development of an [independent French nuclear deterrent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Force_de_dissuasion "Force de dissuasion"). In 1966, he withdrew France from NATO's military structures and expelled NATO troops from French soil.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENuenlistLocherMartin201099–102_302-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTENuenlistLocherMartin201099%E2%80%93102-302">[286]</a></sup>

### Finlandization

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/1970_-_Lenin.jpg/220px-1970_-_Lenin.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1970_-_Lenin.jpg)

A manifestation of the Finlandization period: in April 1970, a Finnish stamp was issued in honor of the 100th anniversary of [Vladimir Lenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin "Vladimir Lenin")'s birth and the Lenin Symposium held in [Tampere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tampere "Tampere"). The stamp was the first Finnish stamp issued about a foreign person.

Officially claiming to be [neutral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neutral_country "Neutral country"), Finland lay in the [grey zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grey-zone_(international_relations) "Grey-zone (international relations)") between the Western countries and the Soviet Union. The [YYA Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finno-Soviet_Treaty_of_1948 "Finno-Soviet Treaty of 1948") (Finno-Soviet Pact of _Friendship, Cooperation, and Mutual Assistance_)<sup id="cite_ref-303"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-303">[287]</a></sup> gave the Soviet Union some leverage in Finnish domestic politics, which was later used as the term "Finlandization" by the West German press, meaning "to become like Finland". This meant, among other things, the Soviet adaptation spread to the editors of [mass media](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_media "Mass media"), sparking strong forms of self-control, [self-censorship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-censorship "Self-censorship") (which included the banning of anti-Soviet books<sup id="cite_ref-304"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-304">[288]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-305">[289]</a></sup>) and pro-Soviet attitudes. Most of the elite of media and politics shifted their attitudes to match the values that the Soviets were thought to favor and approve. Only after the ascent of [Mikhail Gorbachev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev "Mikhail Gorbachev") to Soviet leadership in 1985 did mass media in Finland gradually begin to criticise the Soviet Union more. When the Soviet Union allowed non-communist governments to take power in Eastern Europe, Gorbachev suggested they could look to Finland as an example to follow.<sup id="cite_ref-306"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-306">[290]</a></sup>

For West German conservative politicians, especially the [Bavarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bavaria "Bavaria") Prime Minister [Franz Josef Strauss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franz_Josef_Strauss "Franz Josef Strauss"), the case of Finlandization served as a warning, for example, about how a great power dictates its much smaller neighbor in its internal affairs and the neighbor's independence becomes formal. During the Cold War, Finlandization was seen not only in Bavaria but also in Western [intelligence services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence_service "Intelligence service") as a threat that completely free states had to be warned about in advance. To combat Finlandization, propaganda books and newspaper articles were published through CIA-funded research institutes and media companies, which denigrated Finnish neutrality policy and its pro-Soviet President [Urho Kekkonen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urho_Kekkonen "Urho Kekkonen");<sup id="cite_ref-rislakki_307-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-rislakki-307">[291]</a></sup> this was one factor in making room for the [East-West espionage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War_espionage "Cold War espionage") on Finnish soil between the two great powers.<sup id="cite_ref-rislakki_307-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-rislakki-307">[291]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-308"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-308">[292]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-309"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-309">[293]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-310"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-310">[294]</a></sup>

However, Finland maintained [capitalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitalism "Capitalism") unlike most other countries bordering the Soviet Union. Even though being a neighbor to the Soviet Union sometimes resulted in overcautious concern in foreign policy, Finland developed closer co-operation with the other [Nordic countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nordic_countries "Nordic countries") and declared itself even more neutral in superpower politics, although in the later years, support for capitalism was even more widespread.<sup id="cite_ref-equity_311-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-equity-311">[295]</a></sup>

### Invasion of Czechoslovakia

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/10_Soviet_Invasion_of_Czechoslovakia_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency.jpg/220px-10_Soviet_Invasion_of_Czechoslovakia_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:10_Soviet_Invasion_of_Czechoslovakia_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency.jpg)

The [invasion of Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia "Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia") by the Soviet Union in 1968 was one of the biggest military operations on European soil since [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II").

In 1968, a period of political liberalization took place in [Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic "Czechoslovak Socialist Republic") called the [Prague Spring](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prague_Spring "Prague Spring"). An "[Action Program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialism_with_a_human_face "Socialism with a human face")" of reforms included increasing [freedom of the press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press "Freedom of the press"), [freedom of speech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_speech "Freedom of speech") and [freedom of movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_movement "Freedom of movement"), along with an economic emphasis on [consumer goods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Final_good "Final good"), the possibility of a multiparty government, limitations on the power of the secret police,<sup id="cite_ref-312"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-312">[Q]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVon_GeldernSiegelbaum_313-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVon_GeldernSiegelbaum-313">[296]</a></sup> and potential withdrawal from the Warsaw Pact.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005150_314-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005150-314">[297]</a></sup>

In answer to the Prague Spring, on 20 August 1968, the [Soviet Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Army "Soviet Army"), together with most of their Warsaw Pact allies, [invaded Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia "Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC2008_315-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC2008-315">[298]</a></sup> The invasion was followed by a wave of emigration, including an estimated 70,000 Czechs and Slovaks initially fleeing, with the total eventually reaching 300,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEČulík1998_316-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTE%C4%8Cul%C3%ADk1998-316">[299]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-317"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-317">[300]</a></sup> The invasion sparked intense protests from Yugoslavia, Romania, China, and from Western European countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005154_318-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005154-318">[301]</a></sup>

### Brezhnev Doctrine

In September 1968, during a speech at the Fifth Congress of the [Polish United Workers' Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_United_Workers%27_Party "Polish United Workers' Party") one month after the [invasion of Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia "Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia"), Brezhnev outlined the [Brezhnev Doctrine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brezhnev_Doctrine "Brezhnev Doctrine"), in which he claimed the right to violate the sovereignty of any country attempting to replace Marxism–Leninism with capitalism. During the speech, Brezhnev stated:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005150_314-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005150-314">[297]</a></sup>

> When forces that are hostile to socialism try to turn the development of some socialist country towards capitalism, it becomes not only a problem of the country concerned but a common problem and concern of all socialist countries.

The doctrine found its origins in the failures of Marxism–Leninism in states like Poland, Hungary and East Germany, which were facing a declining standard of living contrasting with the prosperity of West Germany and the rest of Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005153_319-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005153-319">[302]</a></sup>

### Third World escalations

Under the [Lyndon B. Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson "Lyndon B. Johnson") [administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidency_of_Lyndon_B._Johnson "Presidency of Lyndon B. Johnson"), the US took a more hardline stance on Latin America—sometimes called the "[Mann Doctrine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_C._Mann#Mann_Doctrine "Thomas C. Mann")".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993a186–190_320-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993a186%E2%80%93190-320">[303]</a></sup> In 1964, the Brazilian military [overthrew the government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1964_Brazilian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1964 Brazilian coup d'état") of [João Goulart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Goulart "João Goulart") with US backing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993a191_321-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993a191-321">[304]</a></sup> In April 1965, the US sent 22,000 troops to the [Dominican Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominican_Republic "Dominican Republic") in an intervention, into the [Dominican Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominican_Civil_War "Dominican Civil War") between supporters of deposed president [Juan Bosch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_Bosch_(politician) "Juan Bosch (politician)") and supporters of General [Elías Wessin y Wessin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El%C3%ADas_Wessin_y_Wessin "Elías Wessin y Wessin"), citing the threat of the emergence of a Cuban-style revolution in Latin America. The [OAS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organization_of_American_States "Organization of American States") deployed soldiers through the mostly Brazilian [Inter-American Peace Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inter-American_Peace_Force "Inter-American Peace Force").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993a194–97_322-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993a194%E2%80%9397-322">[305]</a></sup> [Héctor García-Godoy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_Garc%C3%ADa-Godoy "Héctor García-Godoy") acted as provisional president, until conservative former president [Joaquín Balaguer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Balaguer "Joaquín Balaguer") won the 1966 presidential election against non-campaigning Juan Bosch.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzigsohn200041–42_323-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzigsohn200041%E2%80%9342-323">[306]</a></sup> Activists for Bosch's [Dominican Revolutionary Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominican_Revolutionary_Party "Dominican Revolutionary Party") were violently harassed by the Dominican police and armed forces.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzigsohn200041–42_323-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzigsohn200041%E2%80%9342-323">[306]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Suharto_at_funeral.jpg/220px-Suharto_at_funeral.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Suharto_at_funeral.jpg)

[Suharto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suharto "Suharto") of Indonesia attending funeral of five generals slain in [30 September Movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/30_September_Movement "30 September Movement"), 2 October 1965

In Indonesia, the hardline anti-communist [General Suharto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suharto "Suharto") wrested control from predecessor [Sukarno](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sukarno "Sukarno") in an attempt to [establish a "New Order"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transition_to_the_New_Order "Transition to the New Order"). From 1965 to 1966, with the [aid of the US](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CIA_activities_in_Indonesia#Anti-communist_purge "CIA activities in Indonesia") and other Western governments,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson2018203_324-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson2018203-324">[307]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimpson2010193_325-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimpson2010193-325">[308]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThaler2015_326-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThaler2015-326">[309]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerry2016_327-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerry2016-327">[310]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBevins2017_328-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBevins2017-328">[311]</a></sup> the military [led the mass killing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indonesian_mass_killings_of_1965%E2%80%9366 "Indonesian mass killings of 1965–66") of more than 500,000 members and sympathizers of the [Indonesian Communist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Indonesia "Communist Party of Indonesia") and other leftist organizations, and detained hundreds of thousands in prison camps under inhumane conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFarid20053–16_329-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFarid20053%E2%80%9316-329">[312]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAarons2007_330-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAarons2007-330">[313]</a></sup> A top-secret CIA report stated that the massacres "rank as one of the worst [mass murders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_murder "Mass murder") of the 20th century, along with the Soviet purges of the 1930s, the Nazi mass murders during the Second World War, and the Maoist bloodbath of the early 1950s."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAarons2007_330-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAarons2007-330">[313]</a></sup> These killings served US interests and constitute a major turning point in the Cold War as the balance of power shifted in Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBevins20202_331-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBevins20202-331">[314]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEScott2017_332-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEScott2017-332">[315]</a></sup>

[Escalating the scale of American intervention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_warfare_in_South_Vietnam,_1963%E2%80%931969 "Joint warfare in South Vietnam, 1963–1969") in the conflict between [Ngô Đình Diệm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ngo_Dinh_Diem "Ngo Dinh Diem")'s [South Vietnamese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Vietnam "South Vietnam") government and the communist [National Front for the Liberation of South Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viet_Cong "Viet Cong") (NLF) insurgents opposing it, Johnson deployed 575,000 troops in Southeast Asia to defeat the NLF and their North Vietnamese allies in the [Vietnam War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam_War "Vietnam War"), but his costly policy weakened the US economy and sparked domestic anti-war protests, which led to the US withdrawal by 1972. Without American support, South Vietnam was [conquered by North Vietnam in 1975](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Saigon "Fall of Saigon"); the US reputation suffered as the world saw the defeat of a superpower at the hands of one of the poorest nations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194–197_117-10"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaFeber1993194%E2%80%93197-117">[111]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Henry_Kissinger_with_Anwar_Sadat_cph.3b13868.jpg/220px-Henry_Kissinger_with_Anwar_Sadat_cph.3b13868.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Henry_Kissinger_with_Anwar_Sadat_cph.3b13868.jpg)

Egyptian leader [Anwar Sadat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anwar_Sadat "Anwar Sadat") with Henry Kissinger in 1975

The Middle East remained a source of contention. Egypt, which received the bulk of its arms and economic assistance from the USSR, was a troublesome client, with a reluctant Soviet Union feeling obliged to assist in the 1967 [Six-Day War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six-Day_War "Six-Day War") and the [War of Attrition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_Attrition "War of Attrition") against pro-Western [Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel "Israel").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStone2010230_333-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStone2010230-333">[316]</a></sup> Despite the beginning of an Egyptian shift from a pro-Soviet to a pro-American orientation in 1972, the Soviets supported Egypt and [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria "Syria") during the [Yom Kippur War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War "Yom Kippur War"), as the US supported Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrenvilleWasserstein1987_334-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrenvilleWasserstein1987-334">[317]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-335"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-335">[318]</a></sup> Although pre-Sadat Egypt had been the largest recipient of Soviet aid in the Middle East, the Soviets were successful in establishing close relations with communist [South Yemen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Yemen "South Yemen"), as well as the nationalist governments of [Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algeria "Algeria") and [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrenvilleWasserstein1987_334-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrenvilleWasserstein1987-334">[317]</a></sup> Iraq signed a 15-year Treaty of Friendship and Cooperation with the Soviet Union in 1972. According to [Charles R. H. Tripp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_R._H._Tripp "Charles R. H. Tripp"), the treaty upset "the US-sponsored security system established as part of the [Arab Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Cold_War "Arab Cold War"). It appeared that any enemy of the Baghdad regime was a potential ally of the United States."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETripp2002_336-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTETripp2002-336">[319]</a></sup> In response, the US covertly financed Kurdish rebels during the [Second Iraqi–Kurdish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Iraqi%E2%80%93Kurdish_War "Second Iraqi–Kurdish War"); the Kurds were defeated in 1975, leading to the forcible relocation of hundreds of thousands of Kurdish civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETripp2002_336-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTETripp2002-336">[319]</a></sup> Indirect Soviet assistance to the Palestinian side of the [Israeli–Palestinian conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict "Israeli–Palestinian conflict") included support for [Yasser Arafat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yasser_Arafat "Yasser Arafat")'s [Palestine Liberation Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization "Palestine Liberation Organization") (PLO).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman2007330_337-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman2007330-337">[320]</a></sup>

In East Africa, a territorial dispute between [Somalia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Somalia "Somalia") and [Ethiopia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethiopia "Ethiopia") over the [Ogaden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ogaden "Ogaden") region resulted in the [Ogaden War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ogaden_War "Ogaden War"). Around June 1977, Somali troops occupied the Ogaden and began advancing inland towards Ethiopian positions in the [Ahmar Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmar_Mountains "Ahmar Mountains"). Both countries were client states of the Soviet Union; Somalia was led by Marxist military leader [Siad Barre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siad_Barre "Siad Barre"), and Ethiopia was controlled by the [Derg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Derg "Derg"), a cabal of generals loyal to the pro-Soviet [Mengistu Haile Mariam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mengistu_Haile_Mariam "Mengistu Haile Mariam"), who had declared the Provisional Military Government of Socialist Ethiopia in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEErlich200884–86_338-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErlich200884%E2%80%9386-338">[321]</a></sup> The Soviets initially attempted to exert a moderating influence on both states, but in November 1977 Barre broke off relations with Moscow and expelled his Soviet military advisers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerrett2016216–217_339-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerrett2016216%E2%80%93217-339">[322]</a></sup> He turned to China and the [Safari Club](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safari_Club "Safari Club")—a group of pro-American intelligence agencies including those of Iran, Egypt, Saudi Arabia—for support.<sup id="cite_ref-340"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-340">[323]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBronson2006134_341-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBronson2006134-341">[324]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-342"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-342">[R]</a></sup> While declining to take a direct part in hostilities, the Soviet Union did provide the impetus for a successful Ethiopian counteroffensive to expel Somalia from the Ogaden. The counteroffensive was planned at the command level by Soviet advisers and bolstered by the delivery of millions of dollars' of sophisticated Soviet arms.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerrett2016216–217_339-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerrett2016216%E2%80%93217-339">[322]</a></sup> About 11,000 Cuban troops spearheaded the primary effort, after receiving hasty training on the newly delivered Soviet weapons systems by East German instructors.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerrett2016216–217_339-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerrett2016216%E2%80%93217-339">[322]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Reuni%C3%B3n_Pinochet_-_Kissinger.jpg/220px-Reuni%C3%B3n_Pinochet_-_Kissinger.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Reuni%C3%B3n_Pinochet_-_Kissinger.jpg)

Chilean leader [Augusto Pinochet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet "Augusto Pinochet") shaking hands with Henry Kissinger in 1976

In [Chile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chile "Chile"), the [Socialist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_Chile "Socialist Party of Chile") candidate [Salvador Allende](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salvador_Allende "Salvador Allende") won the [presidential election of 1970](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970_Chilean_presidential_election "1970 Chilean presidential election"), thereby becoming the first democratically elected Marxist to become president of a country in the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC2003_343-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC2003-343">[325]</a></sup> The CIA targeted Allende for removal and operated to undermine his support domestically, which contributed to unrest culminating in General [Augusto Pinochet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet "Augusto Pinochet")'s [1973 Chilean coup d'état](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_Chilean_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1973 Chilean coup d'état"). Pinochet consolidated power as a military dictator, Allende's reforms of the economy were rolled back, and leftist opponents were killed or detained in internment camps under the [Dirección de Inteligencia Nacional](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direcci%C3%B3n_de_Inteligencia_Nacional "Dirección de Inteligencia Nacional") (DINA). Socialist states—with the exception of China and [Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania "Socialist Republic of Romania")—broke off relations with Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-344"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-344">[326]</a></sup> The Pinochet regime would go on to be one of the leading participants in [Operation Condor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Condor "Operation Condor"), an international campaign of assassination and [state terrorism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_terrorism "State terrorism") organized by right-wing military dictatorships in the [Southern Cone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Cone "Southern Cone") of South America that was covertly supported by the US government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcSherry2011107_345-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcSherry2011107-345">[327]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHixson2009223_346-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHixson2009223-346">[328]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrandin201175_347-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrandin201175-347">[329]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG/200px-Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG)

Cuban tank in the streets of [Luanda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luanda "Luanda"), [Angola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angola "Angola"), 1976

On 24 April 1974, the [Carnation Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnation_Revolution "Carnation Revolution") succeeded in ousting [Marcelo Caetano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcelo_Caetano "Marcelo Caetano") and Portugal's right-wing _[Estado Novo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal) "Estado Novo (Portugal)")_ government, sounding the death knell for the Portuguese Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamann200715–32,_44_348-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamann200715%E2%80%9332,_44-348">[330]</a></sup> Independence was hastily granted to several Portuguese colonies, including [Angola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angola "Angola"), where the disintegration of colonial rule was followed by a civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStockwell1979161–165,_185–194_349-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStockwell1979161%E2%80%93165,_185%E2%80%93194-349">[331]</a></sup> There were three rival militant factions competing for power in Angola: the [People's Movement for the Liberation of Angola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MPLA "MPLA") (MPLA), the [National Union for the Total Independence of Angola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNITA "UNITA") (UNITA), and the [National Liberation Front of Angola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Liberation_Front_of_Angola "National Liberation Front of Angola") (FNLA).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERothschild1997115–121_350-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERothschild1997115%E2%80%93121-350">[332]</a></sup> While all three had socialist leanings, the MPLA was the only party with close ties to the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERothschild1997115–121_350-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERothschild1997115%E2%80%93121-350">[332]</a></sup> Its adherence to the concept of a Soviet one-party state alienated it from the FNLA and UNITA, which began portraying themselves as anti-communist and pro-Western.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERothschild1997115–121_350-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTERothschild1997115%E2%80%93121-350">[332]</a></sup> When the Soviets began supplying the MPLA with arms, the CIA and China offered substantial covert aid to the FNLA and UNITA.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVanneman199048–49_351-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVanneman199048%E2%80%9349-351">[333]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-352"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-352">[334]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-353"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-353">[335]</a></sup> The MPLA eventually requested direct military support from Moscow in the form of ground troops, but the Soviets declined, offering to send advisers but no combat personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVanneman199048–49_351-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVanneman199048%E2%80%9349-351">[333]</a></sup> Cuba was more forthcoming and began amassing troops in Angola to assist the MPLA.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVanneman199048–49_351-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVanneman199048%E2%80%9349-351">[333]</a></sup> By November 1975, there were over a thousand Cuban soldiers in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVanneman199048–49_351-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVanneman199048%E2%80%9349-351">[333]</a></sup> The persistent buildup of Cuban troops and Soviet weapons allowed the MPLA to secure victory and blunt an abortive intervention by Zairean and [South African](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa "South Africa") troops, which had deployed in a belated attempt to assist the FNLA and UNITA.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeigert201156–65_354-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeigert201156%E2%80%9365-354">[336]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg/220px-Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg)

During the [Khmer Rouge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khmer_Rouge "Khmer Rouge") [regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Kampuchea "Democratic Kampuchea") led by [Pol Pot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pol_Pot "Pol Pot"), 1.5 to 2 million people died due to the policies of his four-year premiership.

During the Vietnam War, North Vietnam [used border areas of Cambodia as military bases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sihanouk_Trail "Sihanouk Trail"), which Cambodian head of state [Norodom Sihanouk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norodom_Sihanouk "Norodom Sihanouk") tolerated in an attempt to preserve Cambodia's neutrality. Following [Sihanouk's March 1970 deposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970_Cambodian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1970 Cambodian coup d'état") by pro-American general [Lon Nol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lon_Nol "Lon Nol"), who ordered the North Vietnamese to leave Cambodia, North Vietnam attempted to overrun Cambodia following negotiations with [Nuon Chea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuon_Chea "Nuon Chea"), the second-in-command of the Cambodian communists (dubbed the [Khmer Rouge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khmer_Rouge "Khmer Rouge")) fighting to overthrow the Cambodian government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMosyakov200454_355-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMosyakov200454-355">[337]</a></sup> Sihanouk fled to China with the establishment of the [GRUNK](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GRUNK "GRUNK") in Beijing.<sup id="cite_ref-356"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-356">[338]</a></sup> American and South Vietnamese forces responded to these actions with a [bombing campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Menu "Operation Menu") and a [ground incursion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambodian_campaign "Cambodian campaign"), which contributed to the violence of the [civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambodian_Civil_War "Cambodian Civil War") that soon enveloped all of Cambodia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC2018_357-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC2018-357">[339]</a></sup> US carpet bombing [lasted until 1973](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Freedom_Deal "Operation Freedom Deal"), and while it prevented the Khmer Rouge from seizing the capital, it accelerated the collapse of rural society, increased social polarization,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler200096–98_358-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler200096%E2%80%9398-358">[340]</a></sup> and killed tens of thousands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPower2013_359-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPower2013-359">[341]</a></sup>

After taking power and distancing himself from the Vietnamese,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMosyakov200466_360-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMosyakov200466-360">[342]</a></sup> pro-China Khmer Rouge leader [Pol Pot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pol_Pot "Pol Pot") killed 1.5 to 2 million Cambodians in the [Killing Fields](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Killing_Fields "Killing Fields"), roughly a quarter of the population (commonly labelled the [Cambodian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambodian_genocide "Cambodian genocide")).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELocard2005_361-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTELocard2005-361">[343]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKiernan2003_362-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKiernan2003-362">[344]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeuveline2001102–105_363-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeuveline2001102%E2%80%93105-363">[345]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Peace_Foundation2015_364-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Peace_Foundation2015-364">[346]</a></sup> [Martin Shaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Shaw_(sociologist) "Martin Shaw (sociologist)") described these atrocities as "the purest genocide of the Cold War era."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShaw2000141_365-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShaw2000141-365">[347]</a></sup> Backed by the [Kampuchean United Front for National Salvation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kampuchean_United_Front_for_National_Salvation "Kampuchean United Front for National Salvation"), an organization of Khmer pro-Soviet Communists and Khmer Rouge defectors, Vietnam invaded Cambodia on 22 December 1978. The [invasion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambodian%E2%80%93Vietnamese_War "Cambodian–Vietnamese War") succeeded in deposing Pol Pot, but the new state struggled to gain international recognition beyond the Soviet Bloc sphere. Despite the international outcry at Pol Pot regime's gross human rights violations, representatives of the Khmer Rouge were allowed to be seated in the [UN General Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly "United Nations General Assembly"), with strong support from China, Western powers, and the member countries of [ASEAN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ASEAN "ASEAN"). Cambodia became bogged down in a guerrilla war led from refugee camps located on the border with [Thailand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thailand "Thailand"). Following the destruction of the Khmer Rouge, the national reconstruction of Cambodia was hampered, and Vietnam suffered a punitive [Chinese attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Vietnamese_War "Sino-Vietnamese War").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlocomb2001_366-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlocomb2001-366">[348]</a></sup> Although unable to deter Vietnam from ousting Pol Pot, China demonstrated that its Cold War communist adversary, the Soviet Union, was unable to protect its Vietnamese ally.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_367-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-auto-367">[349]</a></sup> Former U.S. Secretary of State [Henry Kissinger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Kissinger "Henry Kissinger") wrote that "China succeeded in exposing the limits of...\[Soviet\] strategic reach" and speculated that the desire to "compensate for their ineffectuality" contributed to the Soviets' decision to [intervene in Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War "Soviet–Afghan War") a year later.<sup id="cite_ref-368"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-368">[350]</a></sup>

### Sino-Soviet split and Nixon-China visit

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/President_Richard_Nixon_and_Premier_Chou_En-Lai_Shake_Hands_at_the_Nixons%27_Arrival_in_Peking%2C_China.jpg/220px-President_Richard_Nixon_and_Premier_Chou_En-Lai_Shake_Hands_at_the_Nixons%27_Arrival_in_Peking%2C_China.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:President_Richard_Nixon_and_Premier_Chou_En-Lai_Shake_Hands_at_the_Nixons%27_Arrival_in_Peking,_China.jpg)

U.S. President [Richard Nixon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Nixon "Richard Nixon") shakes hands with Chinese Premier [Zhou Enlai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zhou_Enlai "Zhou Enlai") at [Beijing Capital International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beijing_Capital_International_Airport "Beijing Capital International Airport")

As a result of the [Sino-Soviet split](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split "Sino-Soviet split"), tensions along the Chinese–Soviet border [reached their peak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Soviet_border_conflict "Sino-Soviet border conflict") in 1969. United States President [Richard Nixon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Nixon "Richard Nixon") decided to use the conflict to shift the balance of power towards the West in the Cold War through a policy of rapproachment with China, which began with his [1972 visit to China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_visit_by_Richard_Nixon_to_China "1972 visit by Richard Nixon to China") and culminated in 1979 with the signing of the [Joint Communiqué on the Establishment of Diplomatic Relations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Communiqu%C3%A9_on_the_Establishment_of_Diplomatic_Relations "Joint Communiqué on the Establishment of Diplomatic Relations") by [President Carter and Chinese President Deng Xiaoping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visit_by_Deng_Xiaoping_to_the_United_States "Visit by Deng Xiaoping to the United States").<sup id="cite_ref-369"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-369">[351]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005149–152_370-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis2005149%E2%80%93152-370">[352]</a></sup>

### Nixon, Brezhnev, and détente

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Nikolai-Podgornyi-1969-in-Tampere.jpg/220px-Nikolai-Podgornyi-1969-in-Tampere.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Nikolai-Podgornyi-1969-in-Tampere.jpg)

[Nikolai Podgorny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikolai_Podgorny "Nikolai Podgorny") visiting [Tampere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tampere "Tampere"), [Finland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finland "Finland") on 16 October 1969
